Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on What Invalidates Fasting Without Expiation
Enumeration of cases where fasting is invalidated without expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given action that breaks the fast requires only qada' or also kaffara, based on Hanafi criteria of doubt, mistake, and coercion.

Core Idea
When doubt, mistake, or coercion is present, the fast is invalid but no expiation is required.

Fasting is invalidated by many actions, but not all of them demand the heavy expiation (kaffara). The Hanafi school provides a detailed list of scenarios where the fast is broken but only qada' is necessary. This lesson guides you through those cases, highlighting the underlying logic of doubt, lack of deliberate violation, and forced circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the overall ruling pattern
Understand that this passage enumerates actions that break the fast (fasid) but do not require kaffara. The common thread is doubt, mistake, coercion, or lack of deliberate intent.
Contrast with intentional, unforced nullifications which require both qada' and kaffara.
2
Categorize the reasons for no kaffara
Group the cases into categories: doubt (shakk or zann), mistake (forgetfulness, error in judgment), coercion (ikrah), and involuntary actions (sleep, water reaching throat unintentionally).
For example, eating forgetfully followed by intentional eating creates doubt because scholars differ on the effect of forgetful eating.
3
Examine the key legal principle
In each case, the invalidation occurs but kaffara is lifted due to a 'shubha' (legal doubt). The doubt can stem from a difference among scholars (ikhtilaf al-ulama) or from a missing element of full intent.
The Hanafi position is that even if one knows a hadith, the disagreement of earlier scholars creates a valid doubt.
4
Note the distinction between predominant assumption and mere doubt
For cases like breaking the fast thinking sunset had occurred, if one had predominant assumption (ghalabat al-zann), no kaffara; but if merely doubtful, kaffara is required.
This is applied to suhur and intercourse as well.
5
Identify intra-Hanafi differences
In the case of induced vomiting, the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) invalidates even less than a mouthful, but Abu Yusuf required a mouthful (ملء الفم), and this is the mufta bihi view.
The correct view according to al-Tahtawi is that less than a mouthful does not invalidate when re-swallowed.

Source Text

كتاب الصوم
ما يفسد الصوم من غير كفارة
أو آمة بدواء، ووصل إلى جوفه أو دماغه، أو دخل حلقه مطر أو ثلج في الأصح جراحة في الرأس ولم يبتلعه بصنعه، أو أفطر خطأ بسبق ماء المضمضة إلى جوفه، أو أفطر مكرها ولو والاستنشاق أو دماغه وصلية بالجماع، أو أكرهت على الجماع، أو أفطرت خوفا على نفسها من أن تمرض من المرأة المرأة الخدمة، أمة كانت أو منكوحة، أو صب أحد في جوفه ماء وهو نائم أو أكل عمدا الصائم أو شرب بعد أكله ناسيا ولو علم الخبر على الأصح، أو جامع ناسيا ثم جامع عامدا، وصلية بدواء أطلق الدواء فشمل الرطب واليابس؛ لأن العبرة للوصول لا لكونه رطباً أو يابساً، وإنما شرطه القدوري؛ لأن الرطب هو الذي يصل إلى الجوف عادةً حتى لو علم أن الرطب لم يصل لم يفسد ولو علم أن اليابس وصل فسد صومه [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٨/۲] وصل إلى جوفه قوله : "إلى "جوفه عائد إلى الجائفة، وقوله: "إلى دماغه" عائد إلى الآمة، وفي "التحقيق": أن بين الجوفين منفذاً أصليا، فما وصل إلى جوف الرأس يصل إلى جوف البطن. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٨/٢] خوفاً : أي خوفاً يرتقي إلى غلبة الظن، وليس المراد مجرد التوهم. (حاشية الطحطاوي) مطر أو ثلج قيد بهما احترازا عن نحو الغبار فإنه قال في "الهندية": لو دخل حلقه غبار الطاحونة أو طعم الأدوية أو غبار العدس وأشباهه أو الدخان أو ما سطع من غبار التراب بالريح أو بحوافر الدواب وأشباه ذلك، لم يفطر. [حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة: ٦٧٣]
ولم يبتلعه: بل إنما سبق إلى حلقه بذاته، قيد به؛ لأنه إذا ابتلعه بصنعه وجبت الكفارة. أمة إلخ وللأمة أن تمتنع من الائتمار بأمر المولى إذا كان يعجزها عن أداء الفرض؛ لأنها مبقاة على أصل الحرية في حق الفرائض، وإذا علم الحكم في الأمة يعلم الحكم في الحرة بالأولى. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٧٣] أو صب أحد إلخ إنما ذكرت لدفع توهم أن النائم كالناسي، ولا إفطار فيه وليس النائم كالناسي في الحكم حتى لا يفطر؛ لأن الناسي للتسمية تحل ذبيحته؛ لأن الشارع نزله منزلة الذاكر ، بخلاف المجنون والنائم، وحيث ثبت فرق بينهما في بعض الأحكام، فلا يجري حكم أحدهما على الآخر إلا بدليل ، و لم يوجد [حاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٦٧٣] أو أكل عمداً إلخ أي يفسد الصوم ولا تجب الكفارة على من أكل مناسياً ثم أكل عمداً؛ لأنه ظن في موضع الاشتباه بالنظير، وهو الأكل عمداً؛ لأن الأكل مضاد الصوم ساهياً كان أو عامداً، فأورث شبهة، وكذا فيه اختلاف العلماء، فإن مالكاً يقول بفساد صوم من أكل ناسياً [البحر الرائق بزيادة: ٤٥٩/٢] ولو علم إلخ : أي لا تجب الكفارة وإن علم بأنه لا يفطره بأن بلغه الحديث أو الفتوى أولا، وهو قول أبي حنيفة، وهو الصحيح؛ لأن العلماء اختلفوا في قبول الحديث، فإن فقهاء المدينة كمالك لله وغيره لم يقبلوه، فصار شبهة؛ شتهر لأن قول الشافعي له إذا كان موافقاً للقياس يكون شبهة كقول الصحابي البحر الرائق بزيادة: ٤٥٦/٢]

كتاب الصوم
٢١٥
ما يفسد الصوم من غير كفارة
أو أكل بعد ما نوى نهارا ولم يبيت نيته، أو أصبح مسافرا فنوى الإقامة ثم أكل، أو سافر بعد ما أصبح مقيما فأكل، أو أمسك بلا نية صوم ولا نية فطر، أو تسحر أو ناويا من الليل في طلوع الفجر وهو طالع، أو أفطر بظن الغروب والشمس باقية، أو حال فطره شاكا جامع أنزل بوطء ميتة أو بهيمة أو بتفخيذ أو بتبطين أو قبلة أو لمس، أو أفسد صوم غير حالية بجماع أو غيره أداء رمضان، أو وطئت وهي نائمة أو أقطرت في فرجها على الأصح، أو أدخل إصبعه مبلولة بماء أو دهن في دبره أو أدخلته في فرجها الداخل في المختار، أو أو حرقة أو خشبة أدخل قطنة في دبره أو في فرجها الداخل ،وغيبها، أو أدخل حلقه دخانا بصنعه. أو استقاء ولو دون ملء الفم في ظاهر الرواية، وشرط أبو يوسف لله ملء الفم وهو الصحيح، أو أعاد ما ذرعه من القيء وكان ملء الفم وهو ذاكر لصومه، أو وصلية بصنعه غلبه بيان لـ "ما" أكل ما بين أسنانه وكان قدر الحمصة، أو نوى الصوم نهارا بعدما أكل ناسيا قبل إيجاد نيته من النهار، الصوم ثم أكل: أي لا تلزمه الكفارة وإن حرم أكله مراقي الفلاح ٦٧٤] أو تسحر هو من السحور بفتح السين: اسم للمأكول في السحر، وهو السدس الأخير من الليل، وهو مستحب، وقيل: سنة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧٥] شاكا قيد للصورتين من التسحر والجماع (مراقي الفلاح)
في طلوع الفجر: أي لا تجب الكفارة في الصورتين ولكن يأثم إثم ترك التثبت مع الشك، لا إثم جناية الإفطار، وإذا لم يتبين له شيء لا يجب عليه القضاء أيضاً بالشك [مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٦٧٥] بظن الغروب: أراد بالظن: غلبة الظن؛ لأنه لو كان شاكاً تجب الكفارة. [البحر الرائق بحذف: ٤٧٥/٢] على الأصح: أفاد السيد أنه لا خلاف في ذلك على الأصح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٧٦] أو أدخلته أي إصبعها مبلولة بماء أو دهن. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧٧] بصنعه أي متعمداً إلى جوفه أو دماغه لوجود الفطر، ولا تجب الكفارة وهذا في دخان غير العنبر والعود، وفيهما لا يبعد لزوم الكفارة أيضاً للنفع والتداوي، وكذا الدخان الحادث شربه وابتدع بهذا الزمان [مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٦٧٧] ملء الفم: قيده به؛ لأن في الأقل منه روايتان الفطر، وعدمه بإعادته. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧٧] قال الطحطاوي أصحهما عدم الفساد.
Book of Fasting. What invalidates fasting without expiation: Or a slave woman with medicine that reached his stomach or brain, or rain or snow entered his throat in the most correct view; a wound in the head and he did not swallow it intentionally, or he broke his fast mistakenly due to rinsing water reaching his stomach, or he was forced to break his fast, even if by intercourse, or she was forced into intercourse, or she broke her fast out of fear of becoming ill from service – whether slave or married woman – or someone poured water into his stomach while he was asleep, or he ate intentionally after eating forgetfully even if he knew the report according to the most correct view, or he had intercourse forgetfully then intentionally. And the medicine includes both wet and dry because the criterion is reaching, not being wet or dry. Al-Quduri conditioned it because wet usually reaches the stomach, so if he knew that wet did not reach, it does not invalidate, and if he knew that dry reached, his fast is invalidated. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2:438] "To his stomach" refers to a deep wound, "to his brain" refers to a head wound, and in Al-Tahqiq there is an original passage between the two cavities, so what reaches the head reaches the stomach. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2:438] Fear means fear reaching predominant assumption, not mere imagination. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) Rain or snow is a restriction to exclude dust, for it is stated in Al-Hindiyya: if dust from a mill or medicine taste or lentil dust or similar or smoke or dust raised by wind or hooves enters his throat, he does not break his fast. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition: 673] "And he did not swallow it" means it only preceded to his throat by itself; if he swallows intentionally, expiation is obligatory. The slave woman may refuse to obey the master's command if it prevents her from performing the obligatory act, because she is retained on original freedom regarding obligations, and if the ruling is known for the slave, it is known for the free woman a fortiori. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 673] The mention of "or someone poured" is to rebut the notion that a sleeping person is like a forgetful person and does not break his fast, but the sleeping person is not like the forgetful in ruling such that he does not break his fast, because the forgetful in saying the name [of Allah] makes his slaughter permissible due to the Lawgiver treating him like a mindful person, unlike the insane and sleeping; when a difference is established between them in some rulings, the ruling of one does not apply to the other without evidence, and none exists. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with modification: 673] "Or he ate intentionally" means the fast is invalidated but no expiation is required for one who ate forgetfully then ate intentionally, because he assumed in a place of confusion by analogy with the similar act of eating intentionally, for eating contradicts fasting whether forgetfully or intentionally, so it creates a doubt; likewise there is a difference of scholars: Malik says the fast is invalidated for one who eats forgetfully. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with addition: 2:459] "Even if he knew" means no expiation is obligatory even if he knew that it does not break his fast, having heard the hadith or fatwa first, and this is Abu Hanifa's view, which is correct because scholars differed on accepting the hadith; the jurists of Madina like Malik did not accept it, so it became a doubt; because al-Shafi'i's statement, when in agreement with analogy, is a doubt like the Companion's saying. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with addition: 2:456] Book of Fasting. What invalidates fasting without expiation: Or he ate after intending during the day without having made the intention at night, or he became a traveler and then intended to stay and then ate, or he traveled after being a resident and then ate, or he refrained without intention of fasting or breaking the fast, or he ate suhur thinking it was night while dawn was rising, or he broke his fast thinking the sun had set while it remained, or he had intercourse in a state of doubt, or he ejaculated through intercourse with a corpse or animal or through thighing or padding or kissing or touching, or he spoiled the fast of another (non-obligatory) by intercourse or otherwise, or a woman was slept with while sleeping or she inserted a suppository in her vagina according to the most correct view, or he inserted his finger wet with water or oil into his anus, or she inserted it into her vagina according to the chosen view, or he inserted a piece of cotton into his anus or into her vagina and concealed it, or he introduced smoke into his throat intentionally, or he induced vomiting even if less than a mouthful according to the apparent narration, but Abu Yusuf conditioned it being a mouthful which is correct, or he swallowed what he had ejected of vomit that was a mouthful while remembering his fast, or he ate what was between his teeth amounting to a chickpea, or he intended fasting during the day after having eaten forgetfully before making his intention from the day. Then he ate: i.e., expiation is not obligatory although eating is prohibited. [Maraqi al-Falah: 674] Suhur is the food eaten at the last sixth of the night, recommended, and some say sunnah. [Maraqi al-Falah: 675] "In a state of doubt" qualifies the two cases of suhur and intercourse. (Maraqi al-Falah) Regarding dawn: no expiation in the two cases, but he sins for lack of verification with doubt, not for the sin of breaking the fast; if nothing becomes clear to him, qada' is not obligatory either due to doubt. [Maraqi al-Falah with addition: 675] "Thinking sunset" means predominant assumption; if merely doubtful, expiation is obligatory. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with omission: 2:475] "According to the most correct view": it is stated that there is no difference on that. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 676] "Or she inserted" i.e., her finger wet with water or oil. [Maraqi al-Falah: 677] "Intentionally" means deliberately into his stomach or brain, causing invalidation, and expiation is not required; this applies to smoke other than ambergris and aloeswood; for these, expiation would likely be necessary due to benefit and medication, likewise new types of smoke in this time. [Maraqi al-Falah with addition: 677] "A mouthful" restricts it because in less than that there are two narrations regarding invalidation when re-swallowing. [Maraqi al-Falah: 677] Al-Tahtawi said the more correct of the two is that it does not invalidate.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a detailed enumeration of cases where the fast is invalidated (fasad) but no expiation (kaffara) is required. The section expands on the matn of Nur al-Idah with commentary from major Hanafi works. It begins by listing actions such as medicine reaching the stomach or brain, rain or snow entering the throat without intentional swallowing, water from rinsing reaching the stomach accidentally, being forced to break fast, and fear of illness from service for a slave or married woman. The commentary clarifies that the criterion for medicine is reaching the cavity, not wetness; Al-Quduri's condition of wetness is because it usually reaches deeply. It explains that the 'jowf' (hollow) of the head and stomach have an original passage, so what reaches one reaches the other. Fear is defined as predominant assumption, not mere imagination. Dust and smoke are excluded from breaking the fast unless swallowed intentionally. The case of a sleeping person being fed is distinguished from a forgetful person; the sleeping person's fast is invalidated because the Lawgiver treats the forgetful as mindful in some rulings but not the sleeping. Eating forgetfully then intentionally does not require kaffara due to doubt. Abu Hanifa's view that even if one knows the hadith that forgetful eating does not break the fast, no kaffara is required, because the scholars' disagreement creates a doubt. The passage continues with more scenarios: eating after intending during the day without night intention, traveling and changing intention, eating based on incorrect assumption about dawn or sunset, intercourse by mistake or with doubt, ejaculation via unconventional means, spoiling another's fast, and various insertions. In the case of induced vomiting, the apparent narration invalidates even less than a mouthful, but the correct view (Abu Yusuf) requires a mouthful for invalidation when re-swallowing. Throughout, the commentary provides evidence and nuances, emphasizing that these actions break the fast but do not obligate expiation due to doubt, mistake, or lack of deliberate violation.

Key Terms
الجوف (al-jawf): The internal cavity of the body; here specifically the stomach or the hollow of the head, which are considered connected.
الناسي (al-nasi): One who forgets they are fasting; in Hanafi law, forgetful eating does not break the fast, but the text discusses cases where forgetful followed by intentional creates doubt.
الظن (al-zann): Predominant assumption (ghalabat al-zann); here used for determining sunset or dawn, distinguishing from mere doubt (shakk).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, if a fasting person induces vomiting and re-swallows it, what amount must it be for the fast to be invalidated?
A) Any amount
B) Less than a mouthful
C) A mouthful (ملء الفم)
D) Only if it fills the stomach

Key Takeaway
When the fast is invalidated due to doubt, mistake, or coercion, only qada' is required, not kaffara.

Invalidators of Fasting Without Expiation
Lists actions that break the fast but do not require kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which acts break the fast but do not require kaffarah according to the Hanafi school, and distinguish the conditions that trigger kaffarah.

Core Idea
Not all fast-breakers need kaffarah—only deliberate Ramaḍān fast-breaking by intercourse or eating/drinking.

This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates many actions that invalidate the fast but do not incur the heavy penalty of kaffarah. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of fasting. The lesson will walk through the key categories and clarify the conditions under which expiation is avoided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Recognize that kaffarah only applies to specific violations: deliberate intercourse or eating/drinking during a Ramaḍān fast with valid intention. All other invalidators require qada (make-up) but not kaffarah.
2
Categorize the listed invalidators
Group the actions into categories: those related to intention (e.g., not having night intention), travel, uncertainty (e.g., breaking at doubt of sunset), sexual acts (other than intercourse), insertions (finger, cotton, smoke), vomiting, and eating residual food.
3
Note the intra-madhhab difference
Identify that for vomiting, Abu Yusuf conditions a mouthful (mil' al-fam) for the fast to break, while the apparent narration (Imam Muhammad) says any amount breaks it. The text declares Abu Yusuf's view as correct.
This ikhtilaf affects whether qada is required for vomiting less than a mouthful.
4
Understand the legal consequences
For all invalidators listed, the fast is broken (batil) and qada is obligatory. However, kaffarah is not due. Deliberate acts are sinful even without kaffarah.

Source Text

ما يفسد الصوم من غير كفارة أو أكل بعد ما نوى نهارا ولم يبيت نيته، أو أصبح مسافرا فنوى الإقامة ثم أكل، أو سافر بعد ما أصبح مقيما فأكل، أو أمسك بلا نية صوم ولا نية فطر، أو تسحر أو ناويا من الليل في طلوع الفجر وهو طالع، أو أفطر بظن الغروب والشمس باقية، أو حال فطره شاكا جامع أنزل بوطء ميتة أو بهيمة أو بتفخيذ أو بتبطين أو قبلة أو لمس، أو أفسد صوم غير أداء رمضان بجماع أو غيره، أو وطئت وهي نائمة أو أقطرت في فرجها على الأصح، أو أدخل إصبعه مبلولة بماء أو دهن في دبره أو أدخلته في فرجها الداخل في المختار، أو أدخل قطنة في دبره أو في فرجها الداخل وغيبها، أو أدخل حلقه دخانا بصنعه. أو استقاء ولو دون ملء الفم في ظاهر الرواية، وشرط أبو يوسف لله ملء الفم وهو الصحيح، أو أعاد ما ذرعه من القيء وكان ملء الفم وهو ذاكر لصومه، أو أكل ما بين أسنانه وكان قدر الحمصة، أو نوى الصوم نهارا بعدما أكل ناسيا قبل إيجاد نيته من النهار، ثم أكل: أي لا تلزمه الكفارة وإن حرم أكله مراقي الفلاح ٦٧٤] أو تسحر هو من السحور بفتح السين: اسم للمأكول في السحر، وهو السدس الأخير من الليل، وهو مستحب، وقيل: سنة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧٥] شاكا قيد للصورتين من التسحر والجماع (مراقي الفلاح) في طلوع الفجر: أي لا تجب الكفارة في الصورتين ولكن يأثم إثم ترك التثبت مع الشك، لا إثم جناية الإفطار، وإذا لم يتبين له شيء لا يجب عليه القضاء أيضاً بالشك [مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٦٧٥] بظن الغروب: أراد بالظن: غلبة الظن؛ لأنه لو كان شاكاً تجب الكفارة. [البحر الرائق بحذف: ٤٧٥/٢] على الأصح: أفاد السيد أنه لا خلاف في ذلك على الأصح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٧٦] أو أدخلته أي إصبعها مبلولة بماء أو دهن. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧٧] بصنعه أي متعمداً إلى جوفه أو دماغه لوجود الفطر، ولا تجب الكفارة وهذا في دخان غير العنبر والعود، وفيهما لا يبعد لزوم الكفارة أيضاً للنفع والتداوي، وكذا الدخان الحادث شربه وابتدع بهذا الزمان [مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٦٧٧] ملء الفم: قيده به؛ لأن في الأقل منه روايتان الفطر، وعدمه بإعادته. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧٧] قال الطحطاوي أصحهما عدم الفساد.
What breaks the fast without expiation: or eating after intending during the day and did not have intention at night, or became a traveler and then intended residency then ate, or traveled after being a resident and ate, or refrained without intention of fast or intention of breaking, or had pre-dawn meal (suhur) while intending from night at the rising of dawn while it was rising, or broke fast thinking sunset while sun remained, or in the state of his breaking doubtfully engaged in intercourse and emitted by copulating with a corpse or animal or by thigh or by belly or by kiss or by touch, or spoiled the fast of other than Ramadan by intercourse or other, or a woman was copulated while asleep or inserted medication into her vagina according to the soundest, or inserted his wet finger with water or oil into his anus or she inserted it into her vagina according to the chosen, or inserted a cotton ball into his anus or into her vagina and concealed it, or inserted into his throat smoke intentionally, or induced vomiting even if less than mouthful according to the apparent narration, and Abu Yusuf conditioned a mouthful and it is correct, or returned what overcame him of vomit and it was a mouthful while remembering his fast, or ate what was between his teeth and it was the size of a chickpea, or intended fast during the day after eating forgetfully before actualizing his intention from the daytime, then ate: meaning no expiation is obligatory even if his eating is forbidden. Maraqi al-Falah 674. Or suhur: with fath of sin: name for the food eaten at dawn, which is the last sixth of the night, it is recommended, and some said sunnah. Maraqi al-Falah 675. 'Doubtfully' qualifies both cases of suhur and intercourse. Maraqi al-Falah. At rising of dawn: meaning expiation is not obligatory in the two cases, but he sins for lack of certainty with doubt, no sin for the offense of breaking fast, and if nothing becomes clear to him, qada is not obligatory due to doubt. Maraqi al-Falah with addition 675. 'Thinking sunset': he meant overwhelming presumption; because if he was doubtful, expiation becomes obligatory. Al-Bahr al-Raiq abridged 2/475. 'According to the soundest': al-Sayyid said there is no disagreement in that according to the soundest. Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 676. 'Or she inserted it': i.e., her finger wet with water or oil. Maraqi al-Falah 677. 'By his action': i.e., deliberately into his stomach or brain due to occurrence of breaking, and expiation is not obligatory, and this is for smoke other than amber and aloeswood, and in them it is not unlikely that expiation be obligatory for benefit and treatment, similarly the newly invented smoke drunk and innovated in this time. Maraqi al-Falah with addition 677. 'Mouthful': conditioned it because in less than it there are two narrations about breaking and its non-occurrence by returning it. Maraqi al-Falah 677. Al-Tahtawi said: the sounder of the two is that it does not spoil (the fast).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating multiple actions that invalidate the fast but do not require kaffarah (expiation). The author lists scenarios such as: eating after intending to fast during the day without having intended the night before; a traveler who intended residency then ate; one who refrained without any intention; eating while uncertain of dawn; breaking the fast thinking the sun set but it hadn't; engaging in intercourse or similar acts that lead to emission under doubtful circumstances; spoiling a voluntary or make-up fast by intercourse; various insertions or inductions like inserting a wet finger or cotton, smoking deliberately, and vomiting. The commentary clarifies that expiation is not required but the act is still haram. It also notes that Abu Yusuf requires a mouthful of vomit for the fast to break, while the apparent narration says even less. The passage reflects the Hanafi position that not all invalidators incur kaffarah—only deliberate intercourse or eating/drinking during Ramadan with valid intention triggers it.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation mandatory for deliberately invalidating a Ramadan fast by intercourse or eating/drinking without excuse.
ملء الفم (mil' al-fam): A mouthful of vomit; the threshold set by Abu Yusuf for vomiting to break the fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Deliberate intercourse during Ramaḍān
B) Eating after having valid night intention
C) Deliberately vomiting a mouthful
D) Breaking the fast due to travel

Key Takeaway
Many actions invalidate the fast, but only deliberate intercourse or eating/drinking during Ramaḍān with valid intention incur kaffarah; all others require only qada.

No Qada for Unconscious or Insane in Ramadan
Ruling on qada for unconscious/insane persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for a person who is unconscious or insane during Ramadan, and identify the conditions that affect the obligation.

Core Idea
No qada for missed fasts if intention was never possible due to unconsciousness or insanity.

What happens when someone misses the entire month of Ramadan due to unconsciousness or insanity? The Hanafi school carefully examines whether the person had the opportunity to make the intention (niyyah) for fasting. This passage presents the foundational rule and an internal ikhtilaf that affects the final fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subjects
The passage addresses two conditions: unconsciousness (ighma') and insanity (junun). Note that it specifies cases where the condition covers the entire month or part of it.
The text uses 'ghayr mumtadd' for non-extending insanity.
2
State the ruling on qada
The text says clearly: no qada is required for the day in which the unconsciousness occurred, whether it began in the night or during the day, as long as the time for intention (fajr) was missed.
The condition 'bada fawti waqt al-niyyah' is key.
3
Understand the legal rationale
The reason is that the person never had the chance to make a valid intention. Fasting requires intention before dawn, and unconsciousness/insanity prevents that.
This is based on the principle that intention is a condition (shart) for fasting.
4
Note the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf
Shams al-A'imma held that no qada is required even if the person regained consciousness during the day but after the time for intention passed. Al-Fath held that qada is obligatory if the person regained consciousness at any time during the day.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text declares the view of Shams al-A'imma as 'al-sahih wa alayhi al-fatwa' (the correct view and fatwa is upon it).
This is the relied-upon position in the later Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو أغمي عليه ولو جميع الشهر إلا أنه لا يقضي اليوم الذي حدث فيه الإغماء أو حدث في ليلته أو جن غير ممتد جميع الشهر، ولا يلزمه قضاؤه بإقامته ليلا أو نهارا بعد فوات وقت النية في الصحيح.
فصل
يجب الإمساك بقية اليوم على من فسد صومه وعلى حائض ونفساء طهرتا بعد طلوع الفجر، وعلى صبي بلغ وكافر أسلم وعليهم القضاء إلا الأخيرين.
[Commentary:] ولو جميع الخ: أي ولو استوعب الإغماء جميع الشهر. لا يقضي اليوم إلخ لوجود شرط الصوم – وهو النية – حتى لو تيقن عدمها كما لو كان مسافراً أو مريضاً أو متهتكاً يعتاد الأكل في رمضان، لزمه الأول أيضاً. [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٧٧] غير ممتد أي بأن أفاق في وقت النية نهاراً ولم ينو، ووجه وجوب أنه لا حرج في قضاء ما دون شهر [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٧٧] (مراقي الفلاح) ولا يلزمه قضاؤه: أي وإن استوعبه الجنون أو الإغماء شهراً لا يلزمه قضاؤه ولو كان الاستيعاب حكماً بإفاقته ليلاً فقط أو نهاراً بعد فوات وقت النية في الصحيح وعليه الفتوى؛ لأن الليل لا يصام فيه، ولا فيما بعد الزوال كما في "مجموع النوازل" و"المجتبى" و"النهاية" وغيرها، وهو مختار شمس الأئمة، وفي "الفتح": يلزمه قضاؤه بإفاقته فيه مطلقاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح بتصرف: ٦٧٧]
فسد صومه أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان بعذر ثم زال كقتال عدو وحمى زالا، أو من غير عذر. طهرتا إلخ قيد به؛ لأنه في حالة تحقق الحيض والنفاس يحرم الإمساك؛ لأن الصوم منهما حرام والتشب بالحرام حرام، وكذلك لا يجب الإمساك على المريض والمسافر؛ لأن رخصة الإفطار في حقهما باعتبار الحرج، ولو ألزمناهما التشبه لعاد الشيء على موضوعه بالنقض، ولكن لا يأكلون جهراً بل سراً [حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة: ٦٧٨] وعلى صبي بلغ إلخ وكذلك مسافر أقام ومريض بريء ومجنون أفاق [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧٨] الأخيرين: يعني الصبي إذا بلغ بعد طلوع الفجر، والكافر إذا أسلم بعده.
Or was unconscious even if the entire month, except that he does not make up the day in which unconsciousness occurred or occurred in its night, or was insane without extending the entire month, and it is not obligatory for him to make it up by becoming conscious at night or day after the time of intention passed, according to the correct view.
Section: It is obligatory to refrain for the rest of the day for one whose fast became invalid, and for a menstruating woman and woman with postpartum bleeding who become pure after dawn, and for a boy who reaches puberty and an infidel who becomes Muslim, and upon them is qada except the last two.
[Commentary:] ...
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage begins with rulings on unconsciousness and insanity. If a person is unconscious for the entire month or part of it, they do not have to make up the day when the unconsciousness began because the condition of fasting (intention) was present before it. For insanity not covering the whole month, if the person becomes conscious during the day after the time for intention has passed, they do not have to make up that day according to the correct view (mufta bihi). The second section rules that anyone whose fast becomes invalid (for any reason) must still refrain from eating and drinking for the rest of the day as a sign of respect for Ramadan. Similarly, a menstruating woman or woman with postpartum bleeding who becomes pure after dawn must refrain and make up the day later. A boy who reaches puberty during the day and a disbeliever who accepts Islam after dawn must also refrain but are not required to make up that day (the last two). The commentary clarifies exceptions: a traveler, a sick person, etc., are not required to refrain because they are permitted to break their fast, though they should do so privately.

Key Terms
إغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness that prevents a person from being aware and making intention.
جنون غير ممتد (junun ghayr mumtadd): Insanity that does not extend the entire month; the person may have lucid intervals.
نية (niyyah): Intention, a prerequisite (shart) for valid fasting in Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct (mufta bihi) Hanafi view, what is the ruling on qada for a person who was unconscious for the entire month of Ramadan?
A) He must make up all thirty days.
B) He must make up the days only if he regained consciousness briefly during the month.
C) He does not have to make up any day because he never had the opportunity to intend the fast.
D) He must make up the days but only if he was unconscious from before Fajr each day.

Key Takeaway
Unconsciousness and insanity that prevent the formation of intention (niyyah) before Fajr absolve the person from any obligation to make up missed Ramadan fasts, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Obligatory Refraining (Imsak) for Invalid Fasts
Ruling on obligatory imsak and qada after fast invalidation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the persons who must refrain (imsak) for the rest of the day after their fast becomes invalid, and distinguish between those who must make up (qada) and those who are exempt.

Core Idea
Even if your fast breaks, you must still refrain out of respect for Ramadan; but not everyone must make up the day.

This passage presents a crucial principle: the sanctity of Ramadan demands that even those whose fast is no longer valid must abstain from food and drink for the remainder of the day. We will examine the various categories included in this ruling and the important exceptions regarding qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general obligation
The text states: 'يجب الإمساك بقية اليوم' – it is obligatory to refrain for the rest of the day. This applies to any person whose fast became invalid, regardless of the reason.
Imsak here means refraining from all nullifiers (eating, drinking, sexual intercourse, etc.).
2
List the specific persons covered
The text explicitly mentions: (a) one whose fast became invalid (من فسد صومه), (b) a menstruating woman or woman with postpartum bleeding who becomes pure after dawn, (c) a boy who reaches puberty during the day, (d) a disbeliever who accepts Islam during the day.
The phrase 'أطلقه فشمل' in the commentary indicates that 'فسد صومه' includes both excusable and inexcusable invalidation.
3
Separate those who must make up (qada) from those exempt
The text says: 'وعليهم القضاء إلا الأخيرين' – they all must make up the fast except the last two (the boy and the new Muslim).
The last two are: الصبي إذا بلغ after dawn, and the كافر إذا أسلم after dawn.
4
Understand the rationale for imsak
Commentary explains that imsak is wajib to honor the sanctity of Ramadan. Even if the fast is invalid, one must not openly eat/drink. However, a traveler or sick person who is allowed to break the fast does not have to observe imsak because that would contradict their license (rukhsah).
The commentary also notes that such persons should eat/drink privately to avoid public disrespect.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school considers imsak obligatory (wajib). Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider it recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory.
This difference affects the sin of not refraining.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو أغمي عليه ولو جميع الشهر إلا أنه لا يقضي اليوم الذي حدث فيه الإغماء أو حدث في ليلته أو جن غير ممتد جميع الشهر، ولا يلزمه قضاؤه بإقامته ليلا أو نهارا بعد فوات وقت النية في الصحيح.
فصل
يجب الإمساك بقية اليوم على من فسد صومه وعلى حائض ونفساء طهرتا بعد طلوع الفجر، وعلى صبي بلغ وكافر أسلم وعليهم القضاء إلا الأخيرين.
[Commentary:] ولو جميع الخ: أي ولو استوعب الإغماء جميع الشهر. لا يقضي اليوم إلخ لوجود شرط الصوم – وهو النية – حتى لو تيقن عدمها كما لو كان مسافراً أو مريضاً أو متهتكاً يعتاد الأكل في رمضان، لزمه الأول أيضاً. [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٧٧] غير ممتد أي بأن أفاق في وقت النية نهاراً ولم ينو، ووجه وجوب أنه لا حرج في قضاء ما دون شهر [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٧٧] (مراقي الفلاح) ولا يلزمه قضاؤه: أي وإن استوعبه الجنون أو الإغماء شهراً لا يلزمه قضاؤه ولو كان الاستيعاب حكماً بإفاقته ليلاً فقط أو نهاراً بعد فوات وقت النية في الصحيح وعليه الفتوى؛ لأن الليل لا يصام فيه، ولا فيما بعد الزوال كما في "مجموع النوازل" و"المجتبى" و"النهاية" وغيرها، وهو مختار شمس الأئمة، وفي "الفتح": يلزمه قضاؤه بإفاقته فيه مطلقاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح بتصرف: ٦٧٧]
فسد صومه أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان بعذر ثم زال كقتال عدو وحمى زالا، أو من غير عذر. طهرتا إلخ قيد به؛ لأنه في حالة تحقق الحيض والنفاس يحرم الإمساك؛ لأن الصوم منهما حرام والتشب بالحرام حرام، وكذلك لا يجب الإمساك على المريض والمسافر؛ لأن رخصة الإفطار في حقهما باعتبار الحرج، ولو ألزمناهما التشبه لعاد الشيء على موضوعه بالنقض، ولكن لا يأكلون جهراً بل سراً [حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة: ٦٧٨] وعلى صبي بلغ إلخ وكذلك مسافر أقام ومريض بريء ومجنون أفاق [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧٨] الأخيرين: يعني الصبي إذا بلغ بعد طلوع الفجر، والكافر إذا أسلم بعده.
Or was unconscious even if the entire month, except that he does not make up the day in which unconsciousness occurred or occurred in its night, or was insane without extending the entire month, and it is not obligatory for him to make it up by becoming conscious at night or day after the time of intention passed, according to the correct view.
Section: It is obligatory to refrain for the rest of the day for one whose fast became invalid, and for a menstruating woman and woman with postpartum bleeding who become pure after dawn, and for a boy who reaches puberty and an infidel who becomes Muslim, and upon them is qada except the last two.
[Commentary:] ...
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage begins with rulings on unconsciousness and insanity. If a person is unconscious for the entire month or part of it, they do not have to make up the day when the unconsciousness began because the condition of fasting (intention) was present before it. For insanity not covering the whole month, if the person becomes conscious during the day after the time for intention has passed, they do not have to make up that day according to the correct view (mufta bihi). The second section rules that anyone whose fast becomes invalid (for any reason) must still refrain from eating and drinking for the rest of the day as a sign of respect for Ramadan. Similarly, a menstruating woman or woman with postpartum bleeding who becomes pure after dawn must refrain and make up the day later. A boy who reaches puberty during the day and a disbeliever who accepts Islam after dawn must also refrain but are not required to make up that day (the last two). The commentary clarifies exceptions: a traveler, a sick person, etc., are not required to refrain because they are permitted to break their fast, though they should do so privately.

Key Terms
إمساك (imsak): Refraining from eating, drinking, and other fast nullifiers for the rest of the day as a duty of reverence.
صبى بلغ (sabi balagh): A boy who reaches puberty during the daytime of Ramadan.
كافر أسلم (kafir aslam): A disbeliever who accepts Islam during the daytime of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who among the following must refrain (imsak) for the rest of the day but does NOT have to make up the fast?
A) A woman who becomes pure from menstruation after dawn.
B) A traveler who arrives in his hometown mid-day.
C) A boy who reaches puberty after dawn.
D) A person whose fast became invalid due to illness.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory refraining (imsak) after fast invalidation is wajib for all except travelers and the sick; however, only the boy reaching puberty and the new Muslim are exempt from making up the fast (qada).

The Disliked Act of Tasting During Fasting
Lists disliked, permissible, and recommended actions for fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tasting food or drink without swallowing and identify it as one of the seven disliked acts for a fasting person.

Core Idea
Tasting without swallowing is makruh but does not break the fast.

Fasting requires avoiding anything that reaches the stomach, but what about simply tasting? A chef may need to check seasoning, or a mother might test food for her child. The Hanafi school addresses this with a clear ruling that balances necessity and preservation of the fast. This lesson unpacks that ruling from the classical text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific act
Locate the phrase 'ذوق شيء' (tasting something) in the Arabic text. This is the only disliked act explicitly listed in the passage, though the text states there are seven.
The remaining six are not captured due to OCR truncation.
2
Determine the legal ruling (hukm)
The text says 'كره للصائم' (disliked for the fasting person). This places the act in the category of makruh. In Hanafi fiqh, distinguishing between makruh tahrimi and tanzihi is important; here it is generally considered makruh tanzihi when there is a legitimate need, otherwise makruh tahrimi.
The source does not specify the subtype; we rely on standard Hanafi commentaries for further detail.
3
Understand the reason for dislikedness
Tasting risks particles reaching the throat, which could break the fast. Thus, it is discouraged to protect the integrity of the fast. If there is a genuine necessity (e.g., a chef), the dislikedness is reduced.
If swallowing occurs accidentally, the fast breaks and requires qada only.
4
Recognize the broader context
The passage introduces 'seven things' disliked for the fasting person, but only the first is present. Acknowledge that classical Hanafi texts list others such as chewing without swallowing, using miswak after noon, cupping, etc. This lesson focuses on the one available ruling.
The OCR has truncated the list; consult reliable sources for completeness.

Disliked and Not Disliked Actions for the Fasting Person
Enumeration of seven makruh and nine non-makruh actions during fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven disliked and nine non-disliked actions for a fasting person and apply the conditions that change their ruling.

Core Idea
The ruling on kissing, siwak, and tasting food during fast depends on intention, security from desire, and absence of swallowing particles.

This passage from Nur al-Idah provides a comprehensive list of actions that are disliked (makruh tahrimi) for a fasting person and those that are not disliked, along with detailed conditions. Understanding these distinctions prevents unnecessary avoidance of permissible acts and ensures that the fast remains valid while avoiding what may lead to its invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven disliked actions
List the seven actions the author declares makruh: tasting, chewing without excuse, chewing gum, kissing and touching if not secure, gathering saliva and swallowing, and anything thought to weaken (e.g., cupping). Note that these are prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).
The text later qualifies these actions further.
2
Identify the nine non-disliked actions
List the nine actions stated as not makruh: kissing/touching with security, oiling mustache, kohl, cupping/venesection, siwak at any time (even wet), rinsing mouth, sniffing water without wudu, and special cases like tasting for a husband and chewing food for an infant.
Some of these have conditions (e.g., no intent of adornment).
3
Analyze the conditions for chewing gum
Chewing gum is disliked only if particles reach the stomach. Dry gum that does not dissolve is permissible; black gum that dissolves invalidates the fast.
This shows the Hanafi method of restricting general rulings.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on obscene touching
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, kissing/touching is disliked only if there is fear of arousal. However, al-Hindiyyah and al-Muhit state that obscene acts (e.g., naked embracing) are always disliked, even if secure. The mufta bihi position is that obscene touching is disliked absolutely.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Apply the rulings to new scenarios
Using the conditions given, determine the hukm for novel situations: e.g., tasting food for a stranger, using a wet siwak, or kissing with a barrier.
Focus on the underlying illa (e.g., likelihood of invalidation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يكره للصائم، وما لا يكره، وما يستحب كره للصائم سبعة أشياء: ذوق شيء . ومضغه بلا عذر، ومضغ العلك والقبلة والمباشرة إن لم يأمن فيهما على نفسه الإنزال أو الجماع في ظاهر الرواية، وجمع الريق في الفم، ثم ابتلاعه، وما ظن أنه يضعفه كالفصد والحجامة. وتسعة أشياء لا تكره للصائم: القبلة، والمباشرة مع الأمن، ودهن الشارب، والكحل، والحجامة والفصد والسواك آخر النهار ، بل هو سنة كأوله، ولو كان رطبا أو مبلولا بالماء والمضمضة والاستنشاق لغير وضوء بلا عذر كالمرأة إذا وجدت من يمضغ الطعام لصبيها كمفطرة لحيض، أما إذا لم تجد بداً منه، فلا بأس بمضغها لصيانة الولد، واختلف فيما إذا خشي الغبن لشراء مأكول يذاق، وللمرأة ذوق الطعام إذا كان زوجها سيء لتعلم ملوحته؛ وإن كان حسن الخلق فلا يحل لها، وكذا الأمة، قلت: وكذا الأجير. ومضغ العلك: أطلقه وهو مقيد بالذي لا يصل منه شيء إلى الجوف مع الريق، أما إذا كان يصل منه شيء بأن كان أسود مطلقاً مضغ أولا؛ لأن الأسود يذوب بالمضغ أو كان أبيض غير ممضوغ أو كان ممضوغاً، وهو غير ملتئم، فإنه يفسد. والقبلة أطلقها وهي مقيدة بغير الفاحشة؛ لأن القبلة الفاحشة، وهي أن يمص شفتها فتكره على الإطلاق. والمباشرة إلخ: أطلقها فشملت ما إذا كانت فاحشة، وهي أن يتعانقا وهما متجردان ويمس فرجه فرجها أو غيرها، وفي الهندية: الصحيح أن المباشرة الفاحشة تكره وإن أمن بل نقل عن المحيط عدم الخلاف في كراهتها. إن لم يأمن: فإن خشي أحدهما ثبتت الكراهة، قاله السيد في الحاشية. وما ظن أي وكره للصائم ما على ظنه أن فعله يكون سببا لضعفه. ودهن الشارب: بفتح الدال على أنه مصدر، وإنما يباح إذا لم يقصد به الزينة أو تطويل اللحية إذا كانت بقدر المسنون، وهو القبضة، والأخذ اللحية وهو دون ذلك كما يفعله بعض المغاربة ومخنثة الرجال لم يبحه أحد، وأخذ كلها فعل هنود الهند ومجوس الأعاجم. والكحل أي إذا لم يقصد به الزينة، فإن قصدهاكره، واعلم أنه لا تلازم بين قصد الجمال وقصد الزينة، فالقصد الأول: لدفع الشين وإقامة ما به الوقار وإظهار النعمة؛ شكراً لا فخراً، وهو أثر أدب النفس وشهادتها، والثاني: أثر ضعفها. والحجامة: أطلقها وهي مقيدة بالتي لا تضعفه عن الصوم، وينبغي أن يؤخرها إلى وقت الغروب. آخر النهار: قيد بآخره للخلاف ولا خلاف في أوله أنه لا يكره.
Section regarding what is disliked for the fasting person, and what is not disliked, and what is recommended. Seven things are disliked: tasting something, chewing it without excuse, chewing gum, kissing and direct touching if one is not secure in oneself from ejaculation or intercourse according to the apparent transmission, gathering saliva in the mouth then swallowing it, and that which is thought to weaken him like cupping and venesection. Nine things are not disliked: kissing and direct touching with security, oiling the mustache, kohl, cupping and venesection, using siwak at the end of the day (rather it is sunnah like at the beginning) even if it is wet or moistened with water, rinsing the mouth and sniffing water for other than ablution, without excuse like a woman who finds someone to chew food for her child as a menstruating woman, but if she finds no alternative, then there is no harm in her chewing to protect the child, and there is disagreement regarding if one fears loss in buying edible items to taste, and for a woman tasting food if her husband is ill-tempered to learn its saltiness; but if he is good-natured, it is not permissible for her, and similarly for a female slave, I say: and similarly for a hired worker. And chewing gum: he gave it absolutely, but it is restricted to that from which nothing reaches the stomach with saliva, but if something reaches from it, such as if it is black absolutely chewed first because black dissolves with chewing, or white unmasticated or it is masticated and not cohesive, then it invalidates. And kissing: he gave it absolutely, but it is restricted to non-obscene kissing; because obscene kissing, which is when he sucks her lip, is disliked absolutely. And direct touching etc.: he gave it absolutely, so it includes if it is obscene, which is embracing while both are naked and his private part touches her private part or other areas, and in al-Hindiyyah: the correct view is that obscene direct touching is disliked even if secure, rather it is transmitted from al-Muhit that there is no disagreement on its dislikeability. 'If one is not secure': then if one of them fears, dislikeability is established, said by al-Sayyid in the Hashiyah. 'And that which is thought': meaning it is disliked for the fasting person that which in his assumption its action would cause weakness. 'Oiling the mustache': with fatha on the dal as it is a masdar, and it is permitted only if one does not intend adornment or lengthening the beard if it is to the sunnah measure (a fistful), and taking the beard which is less than that as done by some Maghribis and effeminate men, no one permitted, and taking all of it is the act of the Hindus of India and the Magian foreigners. 'Kohl': it is if one does not intend adornment by it; if he intends it, it is disliked. Know that there is no necessary connection between intending beauty and intending adornment; the first intention is to repel defect and establish dignity and show blessing, gratitude not pride, and it is the effect of discipline of the self and its testimony; the second is the effect of its weakness. 'Cupping': he gave it absolutely, but it is restricted to that which does not weaken him for fasting, and one should delay it until sunset. 'End of the day': it was restricted to the end due to disagreement, and there is no disagreement at the beginning that it is not disliked.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah lists the actions that are disliked (makruh tahrimi) for a fasting person, and those that are not disliked. The seven disliked actions are: (1) tasting food without excuse, (2) chewing food without excuse, (3) chewing gum (unless it is dry and no particles reach the throat; if it does, it invalidates the fast), (4) kissing and intimate touching if one fears that it may lead to ejaculation or intercourse (this is according to the apparent transmission; obscene kissing is always disliked), (5) gathering saliva and swallowing it deliberately, (6) anything thought to weaken the body, such as cupping or bloodletting (one should postpone these if possible). The nine actions that are not disliked include: (1) kissing and intimate touching when one is secure from desire (i.e., not fearing arousal), (2) oiling the mustache (without intention of adornment), (3) applying kohl (without cosmetic intent), (4) cupping and bloodletting if they do not weaken the person, (5) using the siwak at the end of the day (it is actually sunnah throughout the day, including at the end), even if it is wet, (6) rinsing the mouth and (7) sniffing water without performing wudu (extra caution not to swallow water). The commentary also addresses special cases: a woman may taste food for her husband if he is ill-tempered to check saltiness; if the husband is good-natured, it is not permissible. Similarly, a mother may chew food for her infant if no one else is available. There is a difference of opinion on whether one may taste a food item to avoid being cheated in a purchase. The Hanafi position on the dislikeability of kissing and direct touch is detailed: if there is fear of arousal, it is makruh; if not, it is not disliked, but obscene touching is always disliked.

Key Terms
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): A level of dislike (makruh) that is close to haram; the action is sinful if done, but not as severe as haram.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent transmission of the ruling from Imam Muhammad's six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah).
العلك (al-'ilk): Chewing gum or similar masticatory substance; the ruling depends on whether any particles reach the stomach.
القبلة والمباشرة (al-qiblah wa al-mubasharah): Kissing and direct physical contact between spouses; the ruling varies based on one's security from desire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following actions is NOT considered disliked (makruh) for a fasting person according to the passage?
A) Tasting food to check its saltiness for a husband with bad temper
B) Chewing gum that dissolves and produces particles that reach the throat
C) Direct touching while secure from ejaculation
D) Gathering saliva in the mouth and swallowing it deliberately

Key Takeaway
The dislikeability of actions during fasting hinges on specific conditions: fear of arousal, presence of particles reaching the stomach, and intention; actions without these conditions are permissible or even recommended.

The Nine Excuses for Breaking the Fast and Recommended Practices
Explains the nine excuses that permit breaking and three recommended acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nine excuses that permit breaking the fast and apply the Hanafi condition that fear of harm must be based on probable cause (ghalabat al-ẓann), not mere doubt.

Core Idea
Breaking the fast is a concession; fasting remains the stronger determination.

This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentaries from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, presents two key topics: the recommended acts for the fasting person and the nine excuses that allow breaking the fast. Understanding these excuses requires careful parsing of each term and its conditions, particularly the requirement of genuine fear of harm based on informed judgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three recommended acts
The text mentions three mustahabb acts: suhur (pre-dawn meal), delaying suhur until close to dawn, and hastening iftar (breaking fast) immediately after sunset, preferably before Maghrib prayer.
These are sunnah mu'akkadah; leaving them is not sinful but loses reward.
2
List the nine excuses
From the passage: illness, travel, coercion, pregnancy, breastfeeding, extreme hunger, extreme thirst, old age, and fighting the enemy (jihad). Each excuse allows a choice (mukhayyar) between fasting and breaking.
The list is exhaustive in the Hanafi school; other excuses like menstruation are handled separately.
3
Analyze the condition for illness
The key condition is 'fear of increase of illness or slow recovery'. This fear must be based on ijtihad (informed judgment) using signs, experience, or the report of a reliable Muslim doctor. Mere suspicion is not sufficient.
The term 'ijtihad' here means reaching a preponderant opinion (ghalabat al-ẓann), not just whim.
4
Distinguish rukhsah from azimah
Breaking the fast is a rukhsah (concession), but fasting is azimah (determination) and superior. The choice exists only when harm is genuinely feared, not for minor discomfort.
This balance prevents unnecessary abandonment of the fast while protecting from genuine hardship.
5
Note special rules for travel and pregnancy/breastfeeding
Travel is an excuse only after the journey has begun; the day of departure is not excused. Pregnant and nursing women must fear for the child's intellect or life, not just their own health.
The text also differentiates between a pregnant woman (hāmil) and a bearer of a load (hāmilah), and between a nursing mother (murḍiʿ) and one actively breastfeeding (murḍiʿah).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عوارض الصوم
كتاب الصوم والاغتسال والتلفف بثوب مبتل للتبرد على المفتى به ويستحب له ثلاثة أشياء: السحور وتأخيره، وتعجيل الفطر في غير يوم غيم.
فصل في العوارض
لمن خاف زيادة المرض أو بطء البرء، والحامل ومرضع خافت نقصان العقل أو الهلاك،
خبر
على المفتى به وكرهها أبو حنيفة؛ لما فيه من إظهار الضجر في إقامة العبادة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٨٢] السحور ولا يكثر منه؛ لإخلائه عن المراد، وهو ذوق مرارة بعض الجوع؛ ليرحم المساكين، وليكون أجره على قدر مشقته كما يفعله المتنعمون مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۸۲] وتعجيل الفطر: ويستحب الإفطار قبل الصلاة، وفي "البحر": التعجيل المستحب التعجيل قبل اشتباك النجوم، ومن السنة عند الإفطار أن يقول: "اللهم لك صمت، وبك آمنت وعليك توكلت وعلى رزقك أفطرت، وصوم الغد من شهر رمضان نويت، فاغفر لي ما قدمت وما أخرت [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦۸۳ العوارض : اعلم أن العوارض تسعة: المرض، والسفر، والإكراه ،والحبل والرضا والجوع والعطش، وكبر السن، وقتال العدو. لمن خاف إلخ [أشار باللام إلى أنه مخير بين الصوم والفطر، لكن الفطر رخصة والصوم عزيمة. (زيلعي على الكنز، البحر الرائق) اعلم أن معرفة ذلك باجتهاد المريض، والاجتهاد غير مجرد الوهم بل هو غلبة الظن عن أمارة أو تجربة أو بإخبار طبيب مسلم غير ظاهر الفسق وقيل: عدالته شرط فلو برئ من المرض، لكن الضعف باق وخاف أن يمرض سئل عنه القاضي الإمام، فقال: الخوف ليس بشيء، كذا في فتح القدير"، وفي "التبيين": والصحيح الذي يخشى أن يمرض بالصوم فهو كالمريض، ومراده بالخشية غلبة الظن كما أراد المصنف بالخوف إياها. [البحر الرائق: ٤٤٢/٢] زيادة أطلق الزيادة فشملت ما إذا كانت بكم بأن ينشأ بالصوم مرض آخر أو كيف بأن يحدث بالصوم اشتداد في المرض القائم. المرض: أطلق في المرض فشمل ما إذا مرض قبل طلوع الفجر أو بعده بعد ما شرع، بخلاف السفر؛ فإنه ليس بعذر في اليوم الذي أنشأ السفر فيه، ولا يحل له الإفطار ، وهو عذر في سائر الأيام. البحر الرائق: ٤٤٣/٢] ولحامل وهي التي في بطنها حمل - بفتح الحاء - أي ولد، والحاملة التي على رأسها أو ظهرها حمل - بكسر الحاء -. (حاشية الطحطاوي) ومرضع ولها شرب الدواء إذا أخبر الطبيب أنه يمنع استطلاق بطن الرضيع وتفطر لهذا العذر. (مراقي الفلاح: ٦٨٥)] التي شأنها الإرضاع، فتسمى به ولو في غير حال المباشرة، والمرضعة التي هي في حال الإرضاع ملقمة ثديها الصبي، ذكره صاحب الكشاف". [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٨٤]
Excuses of fasting. The book of fasting: Bathing and wrapping oneself with a wet cloth for cooling, according to the mufta bihi. Three things are recommended for him: suhur (pre-dawn meal), delaying it, and hastening iftar on a day that is not cloudy. Chapter on the excuses: For one who fears increase of illness or slow recovery; the pregnant woman and nursing mother who fear deficiency of intellect or destruction. Report? According to the mufta bihi, Abu Hanifah disliked it (i.e., the wet cloth?) because it shows impatience in performing worship. [Maraqi al-Falah: 682] Suhur: Do not eat too much of it, because it empties one from the intended purpose, which is tasting some bitterness of hunger to have mercy on the poor, and so his reward is proportional to his hardship, as the refined do. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 282] Hastening iftar: It is recommended to break fast before prayer. In al-Bahr: Hastening that is recommended is before the stars become entangled. From the Sunnah at iftar is to say: 'O Allah, for You I fasted, and in You I believed, and upon You I relied, and on Your provision I break my fast. I intend the fast of tomorrow from Ramadan. Forgive me for what I have done in the past and what I will do in the future.' [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 683] The excuses: Know that the excuses are nine: illness, travel, coercion, pregnancy, breastfeeding, hunger, thirst, old age, and fighting the enemy. For one who fears... He indicated by the lam that he has a choice between fasting and breaking fast, but breaking fast is a concession and fasting is determination. (Zayla'i on al-Kanz, al-Bahr al-Raiq) Know that the knowledge of that is by the ijtihad of the patient; ijtihad is not mere imagination but it is preponderant opinion based on a sign or experience or the report of a Muslim doctor who is not obviously sinful. It is said: his integrity is a condition. If he recovers from the illness but weakness remains and he fears that he will become ill, the Qadi Imam was asked and said: fear is nothing. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Tabyin: The healthy person who fears that he might become ill by fasting is like the sick person. His intent by 'fear' is preponderant opinion, just as the author intended by 'fear'. [al-Bahr al-Raiq: 2/442] 'Increase' – he gave it absolutely, so it includes if it is by quantity, such as that fasting causes another illness arise, or by quality, that fasting causes intensification of the existing illness. 'Illness' – he gave it absolutely, so it includes if he fell ill before dawn or after it after he had started, unlike travel, for it is not an excuse on the day he initiates travel, and it is not permissible for him to break fast; it is an excuse on other days. [al-Bahr al-Raiq: 2/443] For a pregnant woman (hāmil, with fatha on ha) meaning she has a child in her womb, and hāmilah (with kasra on ha) is the one who carries a load on her head or back. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) And a nursing mother (murdi‘) – she may drink medicine if a doctor informs that it will prevent diarrhea of the infant, and she breaks fast for this excuse. (Maraqi al-Falah: 685) She who is in the habit of nursing, even if not actually nursing at the time; and mardi‘ah is the one presently nursing, giving her breast to the child. Mentioned by the author of al-Kashshaf. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 684]
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Nur al-Idah, with extensive commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, covers two closely related topics: the recommended acts for the fasting person and the excuses (عوارض) that permit breaking the fast. The text begins by noting that the mufta bihi (relied upon) position allows bathing and wrapping with a wet cloth for cooling (mari kay al-falah? Actually it is about permissible actions to avoid heat). Then it states three recommended (mustahabb) acts: taking the pre-dawn meal (suhur), delaying it until late, and hastening to break the fast (iftar) immediately after sunset, especially on clear days. Commentary elaborates that suhur should be moderate, and that hastening iftar before prayer is preferred, and includes the recommended supplication. The second part lists nine excuses (عوارض) that allow breaking the fast: illness, travel, coercion, pregnancy, breastfeeding, extreme hunger and thirst, old age, and jihad against the enemy. For each, the existence of a valid excuse gives the person a choice between fasting and breaking, but fasting remains the stronger determination (azimah). The criteria for illness are based on the patient's ijtihad (informed judgment) by signs, experience, or the advice of a reliable Muslim doctor; mere suspicion is not sufficient. Travel is an excuse only for days after travel is initiated, not the day of departure. Pregnant and nursing women break if they fear harm to themselves or the child. The text also distinguishes between a pregnant woman (hāmil) and a bearer of a load (hāmilah), and between a nursing mother (murdi‘) and one actively breastfeeding (murd‘iah). These rulings underscore the Hanafi balance between maintaining the fast and preventing genuine hardship.

Key Terms
العوارض (al-‘awāriḍ): Excuses or circumstances that permit breaking the fast; nine are enumerated: illness, travel, coercion, pregnancy, breastfeeding, hunger, thirst, old age, and jihad.
السحور (al-saḥūr): The pre-dawn meal before fasting; it is recommended (mustahabb) and should be delayed.
تعجيل الفطر (ta‘jīl al-fiṭr): Hastening to break the fast immediately after sunset; recommended, preferably before the Maghrib prayer.
مخير (mukhayyar): Having a choice; the fasting person with a valid excuse may choose to fast or break; but fasting is superior.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT one of the nine excuses (عوارض) that permit breaking the fast?
A) Illness
B) Travel
C) Menstruation
D) Old age

Key Takeaway
The nine excuses are concessions permitting breaking the fast only when genuine fear of harm exists, based on probable opinion.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
10 min
The Nine Excuses for Breaking the Fast
Enumeration of nine excuses with detailed conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the nine Hanafi excuses for breaking the fast and state the conditions for each, including the requirement of predominant opinion (ghalabat al-ẓann).

Core Idea
Breaking the fast is a concession (rukhaṣ) permitted only when fear of harm is based on predominant opinion, not mere doubt.

The Hanafi school recognizes nine specific circumstances that permit a fasting person to break the fast during Ramadan. These are not blanket permissions; each requires a genuine, evidence-based fear of harm. This passage from Nur al-Idah lays out the excuses and their conditions, including important distinctions between illness and travel, the roles of pregnancy and nursing, and the necessity of predominant opinion (ghalabat al-ẓann). We will work through each excuse and the rulings that govern them.

Guided Path
1
List the nine excuses
Start by memorizing the nine excuses mentioned in the text: illness, travel, compulsion, pregnancy, breastfeeding, hunger, thirst, old age, and fighting the enemy.
These are the only recognized excuses in the Hanafi school for breaking a fard fast.
2
Understand the general condition: predominant opinion
The key condition for most excuses is that the fear of harm must be based on ghalabat al-ẓann (predominant opinion), not mere imagination. This can come from personal experience, a reliable sign, or the report of a trustworthy Muslim doctor.
Ijtihad (personal reasoning) is required, but it must be grounded in evidence.
3
Apply the condition to specific excuses: illness, pregnancy, nursing
For the sick person, fear of increased illness or slow recovery must be predominant. For the pregnant and nursing woman, fear of harm to the child's mind or life is considered. The nursing mother includes both biological and wet nurses.
The text distinguishes between a woman who nurses (murḍiʿ) and one actively nursing (murḍiʿah) – the ruling applies to the former even when not currently nursing.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on the healthy person fearing illness
A healthy person who fears becoming ill from fasting is treated like a sick person according to al-Tabyīn, but al-Qāḍī al-Imām ruled that leftover weakness after recovery is not a valid fear. The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) follows al-Tabyīn.
The dispute highlights the importance of predominant opinion versus residual weakness.
5
Analyze the travel ruling and group dynamics
Travel initiated before dawn permits breaking, but travel started after becoming a faster does not. If the majority of travel companions are not fasting or share expenses, breaking becomes preferable for harmony.
The text emphasizes consensus (muwāfaqat al-jamāʿah) as a reason for preferring ifṭār.

فصل في العوارض
لمن خاف زيادة المرض أو بطء البرء، والحامل ومرضع خافت نقصان العقل أو الهلاك، خبر على المفتى به وكرهها أبو حنيفة؛ لما فيه من إظهار الضجر في إقامة العبادة. السحور ولا يكثر منه؛ لإخلائه عن المراد، وهو ذوق مرارة بعض الجوع؛ ليرحم المساكين، وليكون أجره على قدر مشقته كما يفعله المتنعمون. وتعجيل الفطر: ويستحب الإفطار قبل الصلاة، وفي "البحر": التعجيل المستحب التعجيل قبل اشتباك النجوم، ومن السنة عند الإفطار أن يقول: "اللهم لك صمت، وبك آمنت وعليك توكلت وعلى رزقك أفطرت، وصوم الغد من شهر رمضان نويت، فاغفر لي ما قدمت وما أخرت". العوارض : اعلم أن العوارض تسعة: المرض، والسفر، والإكراه ،والحبل والرضا والجوع والعطش، وكبر السن، وقتال العدو. لمن خاف إلخ [أشار باللام إلى أنه مخير بين الصوم والفطر، لكن الفطر رخصة والصوم عزيمة. (زيلعي على الكنز، البحر الرائق) اعلم أن معرفة ذلك باجتهاد المريض، والاجتهاد غير مجرد الوهم بل هو غلبة الظن عن أمارة أو تجربة أو بإخبار طبيب مسلم غير ظاهر الفسق وقيل: عدالته شرط فلو برئ من المرض، لكن الضعف باق وخاف أن يمرض سئل عنه القاضي الإمام، فقال: الخوف ليس بشيء، كذا في فتح القدير، وفي "التبيين": والصحيح الذي يخشى أن يمرض بالصوم فهو كالمريض، ومراده بالخشية غلبة الظن كما أراد المصنف بالخوف إياها. زيادة أطلق الزيادة فشملت ما إذا كانت بكم بأن ينشأ بالصوم مرض آخر أو كيف بأن يحدث بالصوم اشتداد في المرض القائم. المرض: أطلق في المرض فشمل ما إذا مرض قبل طلوع الفجر أو بعده بعد ما شرع، بخلاف السفر؛ فإنه ليس بعذر في اليوم الذي أنشأ السفر فيه، ولا يحل له الإفطار ، وهو عذر في سائر الأيام. ولحامل وهي التي في بطنها حمل - بفتح الحاء - أي ولد، والحاملة التي على رأسها أو ظهرها حمل - بكسر الحاء -. (حاشية الطحطاوي) ومرضع ولها شرب الدواء إذا أخبر الطبيب أنه يمنع استطلاق بطن الرضيع وتفطر لهذا العذر. (مراقي الفلاح: ٦٨٥)] التي شأنها الإرضاع، فتسمى به ولو في غير حال المباشرة، والمرضعة التي هي في حال الإرضاع ملقمة ثديها الصبي، ذكره صاحب الكشاف". [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٨٤] أو المرض على نفسها نسبا كان أو رضاعا والخوف المعتبر ما كان مستندا لغلبة الظن بتجربة أو إخبار طبيب مسلم حاذق عدل، ولمن حصل له عطش شديد أو أي بتجربة سابقة جوع يخاف منه الهلاك، وللمسافر الفطر، وصومه أحب إن لم يضره، ولم تكن عامة رفقته مفطرين، ولا مشتركين في النفقة، فإن كانوا مشتركين، أو مفطرين في النفقة فالأفضل فطره موافقة للجماعة، ولا يجب الإيصاء على من مات قبل زوال عذره بمرض وسفر ونحوه كما تقدم، وقضوا ما قدروا على قضائه بقدر الإقامة والصحة، ولا يشترط التتابع في القضاء، . نسبا كان أو :رضاعا يفيد أنه لا فرق بين الأم والظئر، أما الظئر ؛ فلأن الإرضاع واجب عليها بالعقد، وأما الأم؛ فلوجوبه ديانة مطلقاً، وقضاء إذا كان الأب معسراً أو كان الولد لا يرضع من غيرها، وبهذا اندفع ما في " الذخيرة" من أن المراد بالمرضع الظئر لا الأم ؛ فإن الاب يستاجر غيرها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٨٥] الهلاك أو نقصان العقل أو ذهاب بعض الحواس. مراقي الفلاح: ٦٨٥] للمسافر الفطر: أراد به المسافر الذي أنشأ السفر قبل طلوع الفجر؛ إذ لا يباح له الفطر بإنشائه بعد ما أصبح صائماً، بخلاف ما لو حل به مرض بعده فله الفطر. مراقي الفلاح: ٢٨٦] إن لم يضره أراد بالضرر الذي ليس فيه خوف الهلاك؛ لأن ما فيه خوف الهلاك بسبب الصوم، فالإفطار في مثله واجب؛ لا أنه أفضل [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٨٦] ولم تكن عامة قيد بالعامة، فأفاد أن القليل لو أفطر لا يكون الفطر أفضل. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٨٦] موافقة للجماعة عدل إليه عن قول صاحب "البحر": "إذا كانت النفقة مشتركة، فالفطر أفضل"؛ لما أن ضرر المال كضرر النفس لما قاله في "النهر": إن التعليل بموافقة الجماعة أولى، وأما لزوم ضرر المال بضياعه بصومه فممنوع، لجواز أن يأخذ نصيبه ويبقيه أو يكون سمحاً يتجاوز عن نصيبه. [حاشية الطحطاوي بحذف: ٦٨٦] ولا يجب الإيصاء إلخ : أي إذا أفطر مريض أو مسافر أو من به عذر من الأعذار المبيحة ومات و لم يزل . عذره، فلا يجب عليه أن يوصي ،ورثته، ولا غيرهم بأداء كفارة ما أفطره. وقضوا ما قدروا ينبغي أن يستثنى الأيام المنهية؛ لأنه عاجز عن القضاء فيها شرعاً، فلو فاته عشرة أيام فقدر على خمسة أدى فديتها فقط، وفائدة لزوم القضاء وجوب الوصية بالإطعام، وينفذ ذلك من الثلث بشرط أن لا يكون في التركة دين من ديون العباد، حتى لو كان ينفذ ذلك من ثلث الباقي، إلا إذا لم يكن له وارث، فحينئذ ينفذ من جميع ما بقي منه
Section on the impediments (ʿawāriḍ). For one who fears an increase in illness or slow recovery, and for a pregnant woman or a nursing mother who fears mental defect or destruction, the [relied-upon] position is that [breaking the fast] is permissible (ʿalā al-muftā bihī) and Abū Ḥanīfah disliked it because it shows discontent in performing worship. [On] suḥūr: do not eat excessively because it defeats the purpose, which is to taste some bitterness of hunger in order to have mercy on the poor and so that one's reward is proportional to hardship, as is done by those accustomed to comfort. Hastening the ifṭār: it is recommended to break the fast before prayer. In al-Baḥr, the recommended hastening is before the stars become entangled. From the sunnah at ifṭār is to say: 'O Allah, for You I fasted, in You I believed, upon You I relied, and with Your provision I break my fast. I intend to fast tomorrow of Ramadan. Forgive me my past and future [sins].' The impediments: Know that the impediments are nine: illness, travel, compulsion, pregnancy, breastfeeding/رضاع, hunger, thirst, old age, and fighting the enemy. For one who fears [etc.] [The lām indicates that he has a choice between fasting and breaking, but breaking is a concession and fasting is determination. (Zaylaʿī ʿalā al-Kanz, al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq)] Know that knowing this is by the ijtihād of the sick person, and ijtihād is not mere delusion but rather predominant opinion based on a sign, experience, or the report of a Muslim doctor who is not openly sinful. It was said: his uprightness (ʿadālah) is a condition. If one recovers from illness but weakness remains and he fears falling ill again, this was asked of the Chief Judge (al-Qāḍī al-Imām), and he said: fear is not a consideration. Thus in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. In al-Tabyīn, a healthy person who fears falling ill from fasting is like the sick, and by 'fear' he means predominant opinion, just as the author meant by 'fear' that. 'Increase' is absolute and includes when a different illness arises due to fasting or when the existing illness intensifies. 'Illness' is absolute and includes when one falls ill before dawn or after dawn after having begun [the fast], unlike travel: for it is not an excuse on the day one initiates travel, and it is not permissible to break, but it is an excuse on other days. (al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq) And for a pregnant woman: she is one who has a pregnancy in her belly – with fatḥ on the ḥā – meaning a child, while 'al-ḥāmilah' is one who carries a load on her head or back – with kasr on the ḥā. (Ḥāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī) And for a nursing mother: she may take medicine if the doctor reports that it prevents diarrhea in the infant, and she breaks for this excuse. (Marāqī al-Falāḥ) [She is] one whose characteristic is nursing, thus she is called this even when not actually nursing. The one who is actually nursing (al-murḍiʿah) is she who is in the act of nursing, putting her breast in the infant's mouth. Mentioned by the author of al-Kashshāf. (Ḥāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī) Or illness upon herself, whether by lineage or fosterage. The fear that is considered is that which is based on predominant opinion from experience or the report of a skilled, upright Muslim doctor. And for one who experiences severe thirst or [or from previous experience] hunger from which he fears destruction, and for the traveler, breaking the fast [is allowed] and fasting is preferable if it does not harm him, and if the majority of his traveling companions are not fasting, and they are not sharing expenses. If they share expenses or are all not fasting, then breaking is better in order to be in agreement with the group. And it is not necessary to make a will for one who dies before his excuse (such as illness or travel) ends, as previously mentioned. And they must make up what they were able to, according to the duration of health and residence, and consecutive fasting is not required in making up. [The phrase] 'by lineage or fosterage' indicates that there is no difference between the mother and the wet nurse. As for the wet nurse, because nursing is obligatory upon her by contract; as for the mother, because it is obligatory religiously (diyānah) unconditionally, and judicially (qaḍāʾ) if the father is insolvent or the child will not suckle from anyone else. With this, what is in al-Dhakhīrah is refuted, that by 'nursing mother' is meant the wet nurse, not the mother, because the father can hire someone else. (Ḥāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī) Destruction or mental defect or loss of some senses. (Marāqī al-Falāḥ) For the traveler, breaking [is allowed]: what is meant is the traveler who initiated travel before dawn; it is not permissible for him to break by initiating travel after becoming a faster, unlike if illness befalls him afterwards, then he may break. (Marāqī al-Falāḥ) 'If it does not harm him': what is meant is harm that does not involve fear of destruction, because that which involves fear of destruction due to fasting makes breaking obligatory, not merely preferable. (Ḥāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī) 'And if the majority are not' — the restriction to 'majority' indicates that if a few break, then breaking is not preferable. (Ḥāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī) 'In agreement with the group' — this was chosen over the statement of the author of al-Baḥr: 'If expenses are shared, then breaking is preferable', because harm to wealth is like harm to the self, as stated in al-Nahr: the reasoning of agreement with the group is more appropriate. As for the claim of harm to wealth by losing it due to fasting, it is rejected because he may take his share and save it, or may be generous and forgo his share. (Ḥāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī, abridged) 'And it is not necessary to make a will, etc.': that is, if a sick person, a traveler, or one with any permissible excuse breaks his fast and dies before his excuse ends, he does not have to will his heirs or others to pay expiation for what he broke. 'And they make up what they were able' — it should be excepted the prohibited days because he is legally unable to make up on them. So if he missed ten days and was able to [make up] five, he only pays the fidyah for those five. The benefit of the obligation to make up is the obligation of willing to feed [the poor], and that is executed from one-third [of the estate] on condition that there is no debt owed to people in the estate. If there is, then it is executed from one-third of the remainder, unless he has no heir, in which case it is executed from the entire remainder.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the impediments (ʿawāriḍ) to fasting. It begins by listing the nine valid excuses that allow one to break the fast: illness, travel, compulsion, pregnancy, breastfeeding, hunger, thirst, old age, and fighting the enemy. The author then clarifies the conditions for these excuses. For the sick person, the fear of increased illness must be based on predominant opinion (ghalabat al-ẓann), not mere conjecture, and can stem from personal experience, a sign, or the report of a Muslim doctor who is not openly sinful. The text distinguishes between illness occurring before fasting (allows breaking) and initiating travel during a fast (does not allow breaking on that day). For pregnant and nursing women, fear of harm to the child's mind or life is considered, and again the fear must be based on predominant opinion from experience or a reliable doctor. The nursing mother includes both the biological mother and a wet nurse, but the ruling differs based on obligation. For travelers, breaking is permitted but fasting is preferred if no harm occurs; however, if the travel companions are mostly not fasting or share expenses, breaking becomes preferable for harmony. Finally, the passage covers making up missed fasts: if one dies before the excuse ends, no will is necessary; if one can make up only part of what was missed, one pays fidyah for the remainder. The text emphasizes that consecutive fasting (tatābuʿ) is not required in making up.

Key Terms
العوارض (al-ʿawāriḍ): Impediments or accidental circumstances that permit breaking the fast; enumerated as nine in this text.
الخوف (al-khawf): Predominant fear (ghalabat al-ẓann) of increased illness or harm, based on evidence such as experience or a reliable doctor's report.
المرضع (al-murḍiʿ): A woman who nurses a child, whether she is the biological mother or a wet nurse; the term applies even when not actively nursing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, how many excuses (awarid) are there for breaking the fast?
A) 5
B) 7
C) 9
D) 11

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits breaking the fast for nine specific excuses, provided the fear of harm is based on predominant opinion, not mere doubt.
