I'tikaf: Definition and Types
Definition and classification of i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of i'tikaf, identify its three categories, and apply the condition for the mosque.

Core Idea
I'tikaf requires a mosque with regular congregation; it is sunnah kifayah in Ramadan, wajib if vowed, and mustahabb otherwise.

I'tikaf is a spiritual retreat in the mosque that the Prophet ﷺ never abandoned. The Hanafi school defines it precisely: it must be performed in a mosque that holds regular congregational prayers. This lesson covers the definition, the three types of i'tikaf, and the key condition regarding the mosque.

Guided Path
1
Define i'tikaf and its essential elements
Identify the core components: staying (al-iqama), intention (al-niyya), and the location (a mosque with regular congregation for the five daily prayers).
The intention is what distinguishes worship from mere rest.
2
Classify the three categories of i'tikaf
List the types: 1) Wajib (when vowed), 2) Sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah (last ten days of Ramadan), 3) Mustahabb (any other time). Understand that the communal sunnah lifts the obligation if performed by some.
Only i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan carries this communal emphasis.
3
Apply the mosque condition
According to the chosen opinion (al-mukhtar), i'tikaf is valid only in a mosque where the five daily prayers are established with congregation. This applies to all types, not just wajib.
Abu Yusuf disagrees: he requires congregation only for wajib i'tikaf.
4
Recognize the exception for women
A woman performs i'tikaf in the 'mosque of her house' – the place she designates for prayer. She should not leave without excuse; otherwise it invalidates her i'tikaf.
This ruling maintains the spirit of i'tikaf while accommodating her domestic responsibilities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاعتكاف أحكام الاعتكاف هو الإقامة بنيته في مسجد تقام فيه الجماعة بالفعل للصلوات الخمس، فلا يصح في مسجد لا تقام فيه الجماعة للصلاة على المختار وللمرأة الاعتكاف في مسجد بيتها، وهو محل عينته للصلاة فيه، والاعتكاف على ثلاثة أقسام: واجب في المنذور، وسنة كفاية مؤكدة في العشر الأخير من رمضان ومستحب فيما سواه، والصوم شرط لصحة المنذور فقط، وأقله نفلا مدة يسيرة ولو كان ماشياً على المفتى به، ولا يخرج الاعتكاف المنذور ليس شرطا في النفل وصلبة [؟] من نوى الاعتكاف منه إلا لحاجة شرعية كالجمعة أو طبعية كالبول، أو ضرورية كانهدام المسجد، ... ومعتكفه والعيدين على المختار وعن أبي يوسف الاعتكاف الواجب لا يجوز في غير مسجد الجماعة، والنفل يجوز. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٩٩] في مسجد بيتها ولا تخرج منه إذا اعتكفت فلو خرجت لغير عذر يفسد واجبه، وينتهي نفله، ولو اعتكفت في المسجد فظاهرُ ما في "النهاية" أنه يكره تنزيهاً، وينبغي على قياس ما صرحوا به من أن المختار منعهنّ من الخروج في الصلوات كلها أن لا يتردد في منعهن من الاعتكاف في المسجد. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٩٩] وسنة كفاية إلخ قال الزاهدي: عجباً للناس كيف تركوا الاعتكاف، وقد كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يفعل الشيء ويتركه، ولم يترك الاعتكاف منذ دخل المدينة إلى أن مات فهذه المواظبة المقرونة بعدم الترك مرة لما اقترنت بعدم الإنكار على من لم يفعله من الصحابة من كانت دليل السنية، أي على الكفاية، وإلا كانت دليل الوجوب على الأعيان. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۷۰۰] فيما سواه أي في أي وقت شاء سوى العشر الأخير، ولم يكن منذوراً. [مراقي الفلاح: ۷۰۱] لصحة المنذور فلو قال عليّ أن أعتكف شهراً بغير صوم عليه أن يعتكف ويصوم، فإن قيل: لو كان شرطا لكان شرط انعقاد ودوام ، وليس كذلك ؛ لصحة الشروع فيه ليلا وكذا يبقى في الليل ولا صوم؟ قلنا: الشرائط إنما تعتبر بحسب الإمكان ولا إمكان في الليل فيسقط للتعذر وجعلت الليالي تابعة للأيام كالشرب والطريق في بيع الأرض، ألا ترى أن صلاة المستحاضة تصح مع السيلان، وإن عدم الشرط للتعذر، وكذا الخروج والبول لا ينافيه للعجز مع أن الركن أقوى من الشرط. (كفاية) [وحاشية الطحطاوي] يسيرة: غير محددة، فيحصل بمجرد المكث مع النية. [مراقي الفلاح: ۷۰۲] ماشياً: أي ماراً غير جالس في المسجد ولو ليلاً، وهو حيلة من أراد الدخول والخروج من باب آخر في المسجد حتى لا يجعله طريقاً. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧٠٢] للغائط
The chapter of I'tikaf. Rulings of I'tikaf. It is staying with intention in a mosque in which congregation is established in practice for the five prayers. So it is not valid in a mosque in which congregation for prayer is not established, according to the chosen opinion. And for a woman, i'tikaf is in the mosque of her house, which is the place she designated for prayer. I'tikaf is of three types: obligatory in the vowed, sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah in the last ten days of Ramadan, and mustahabb in other than that. Fasting is a condition for the validity of the obligatory only. The minimum of optional i'tikaf is a short period, even if walking, according to the relied-upon opinion. And the vowed i'tikaf does not... [uncertain]... except for a lawful need like Jumu'ah, or natural like urine, or necessary like the mosque collapsing... and his place of i'tikaf, and the two Eids, according to the chosen opinion. And from Abu Yusuf: obligatory i'tikaf is not permissible in other than a mosque with congregation, but optional is permissible. [Maraqi al-Falah: 699] In the mosque of her house, and she should not leave from it if she performs i'tikaf. If she leaves without an excuse, it invalidates her obligatory i'tikaf and terminates her optional one. And if she performs i'tikaf in the mosque, the apparent of what is in al-Nihayah is that it is makruh tanzihan. And it is fitting, on the analogy of what they stated that the chosen opinion prevents them from going out for all prayers, that there be no hesitation in preventing them from i'tikaf in the mosque. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 699] And sunnah kifayah etc. Al-Zahidi said: Amazing at the people how they abandoned i'tikaf, while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to do something and leave it, but he did not leave i'tikaf from when he entered Madinah until he died. This consistent practice coupled with not leaving it once, coupled with the lack of disapproval from the Companions who did not do it, is evidence of it being sunnah, i.e., on the level of sufficiency (kifayah), otherwise it would be evidence of individual obligation. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 700] 'In other than that' means in any time he wishes except the last ten days, and it is not vowed. [Maraqi al-Falah: 701] For the validity of the obligatory: if he says 'Upon me is to perform i'tikaf for a month without fasting', he must perform i'tikaf and fast. If it is said: If fasting were a condition, it would be a condition for initiation and continuity, but it is not so because it is valid to begin i'tikaf at night, and likewise he remains during the night without fasting. We say: Conditions are considered according to possibility, and there is no possibility at night, so it falls due to impossibility, and the nights are made dependent on the days like the stream and the road in the sale of land. Do you not see that the prayer of a woman with istihadah is valid despite the flow, because the condition is absent due to impossibility. Similarly, exiting and urinating do not oppose it due to inability, even though the pillar is stronger than the condition. (Kifayah) [and Hashiyah al-Tahtawi] 'Short period': unspecified, so it is achieved by just staying with the intention. [Maraqi al-Falah: 702] 'Walking': meaning passing through, not sitting in the mosque, even at night, and it is a stratagem for one who wants to enter and exit from another door in the mosque so that he does not make it a thoroughfare. [Maraqi al-Falah: 702] For feces.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on i'tikaf, providing a comprehensive definition and classification. The author defines i'tikaf as staying with intention in a mosque that has regular congregation for the five prayers; this condition applies to all types of i'tikaf according to the chosen opinion. For women, i'tikaf is in their home prayer area. I'tikaf is divided into three categories: obligatory if vowed, sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah for the last ten days of Ramadan, and mustahabb at other times. Fasting is only a condition for obligatory i'tikaf, not for voluntary. The minimum duration for voluntary i'tikaf is a short period, even just passing through. The passage then discusses that one may exit for lawful needs. A dispute from Abu Yusuf is noted: he requires congregational mosque only for obligatory i'tikaf, while the chosen opinion requires it for all. The evidence for i'tikaf being sunnah is derived from the Prophet's consistent practice and the lack of disapproval from Companions who did not do it, indicating it is a communal sunnah. The condition of fasting for obligatory i'tikaf is justified by analogy: nights are dependent on days, and the impossibility of fasting at night drops the condition, similar to the prayer of a mustahadah.

Key Terms
اعتكاف (i'tikaf): Staying in a mosque with intention for worship.
سنة كفاية (sunnah kifayah): A communal sunnah; if performed by some, the obligation is lifted from all; if abandoned by all, sin incurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion, i'tikaf is valid in which of the following?
A) Any mosque, even one without congregation.
B) Only in the Prophet's mosque in Madinah.
C) A mosque where the five daily prayers are held with congregation.
D) Only in one's home.

Key Takeaway
The mosque condition is decisive: all i'tikaf (voluntary or obligatory) requires a mosque that holds regular congregation for the five prayers.

I'tikaf: Conditions and Evidence
Conditions and evidence for i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of fasting for obligatory i'tikaf, explain why nights are included, and analyze the hadith evidence that i'tikaf is sunnah kifayah.

Core Idea
Fasting is required only for vowed i'tikaf; the Prophet's consistent practice proves it is a communal sunnah.

The previous lesson defined i'tikaf and its types; now we delve into specific conditions: fasting for obligatory i'tikaf, the minimum duration, and the powerful evidence from the Prophet's ﷺ practice that makes i'tikaf in the last ten days a communal sunnah. We also explore the justification for including nights despite the fasting condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fasting condition for obligatory i'tikaf
The text explicitly states: 'والصوم شرط لصحة المنذور فقط' – fasting is a condition only for the validity of vowed (obligatory) i'tikaf.
Voluntary i'tikaf does not require fasting.
2
Explain why nights are included despite the impossibility of fasting at night
The condition of fasting is considered only when possible. Nights cannot be fasted, so they are made dependent on the days, similar to ancillary rights in a sale (sharb and tariq). The analogy of mustahadah's prayer is cited.
This is a subtle usul principle: conditions are relaxed when impossible.
3
Determine the minimum duration for optional i'tikaf
The text says 'وأقله نفلا مدة يسيرة ولو كان ماشياً على المفتى به' – the minimum is a short period, even if walking (passing through).
This is a practical facilitation; one can achieve i'tikaf by simply passing through with intention.
4
Analyze the evidence that i'tikaf in the last ten days is sunnah kifayah
Al-Zahidi presents proof: The Prophet ﷺ never abandoned i'tikaf from his arrival in Madinah until his death. This consistent practice, coupled with the fact that some Companions did not do it and he did not criticize them, indicates it is sunnah, not obligatory. The lack of criticism for those who did not do it shows it is a communal sunnah (kifayah).
If it were fard ayn, the Prophet would have commanded it and criticized omission.
5
Note the dispute with Abu Yusuf on the mosque condition? Not repeated; this lesson focuses on fasting and evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If she leaves without an excuse, it invalidates her obligatory i'tikaf and terminates her optional one. And if she performs i'tikaf in the mosque, the apparent of what is in al-Nihayah is that it is makruh tanzihan. And it is fitting, on the analogy of what they stated that the chosen opinion prevents them from going out for all prayers, that there be no hesitation in preventing them from i'tikaf in the mosque. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 699] And sunnah kifayah etc. Al-Zahidi said: Amazing at the people how they abandoned i'tikaf, while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to do something and leave it, but he did not leave i'tikaf from when he entered Madinah until he died. This consistent practice coupled with not leaving it once, coupled with the lack of disapproval from the Companions who did not do it, is evidence of it being sunnah, i.e., on the level of sufficiency (kifayah), otherwise it would be evidence of individual obligation. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 700] 'In other than that' means in any time he wishes except the last ten days, and it is not vowed. [Maraqi al-Falah: 701] For the validity of the obligatory: if he says 'Upon me is to perform i'tikaf for a month without fasting', he must perform i'tikaf and fast. If it is said: If fasting were a condition, it would be a condition for initiation and continuity, but it is not so because it is valid to begin i'tikaf at night, and likewise he remains during the night without fasting. We say: Conditions are considered according to possibility, and there is no possibility at night, so it falls due to impossibility, and the nights are made dependent on the days like the stream and the road in the sale of land. Do you not see that the prayer of a woman with istihadah is valid despite the flow, because the condition is absent due to impossibility. Similarly, exiting and urinating do not oppose it due to inability, even though the pillar is stronger than the condition. (Kifayah) [and Hashiyah al-Tahtawi] 'Short period': unspecified, so it is achieved by just staying with the intention. [Maraqi al-Falah: 702] 'Walking': meaning passing through, not sitting in the mosque, even at night, and it is a stratagem for one who wants to enter and exit from another door in the mosque so that he does not make it a thoroughfare. [Maraqi al-Falah: 702] For feces.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on i'tikaf, providing a comprehensive definition and classification. The author defines i'tikaf as staying with intention in a mosque that has regular congregation for the five prayers; this condition applies to all types of i'tikaf according to the chosen opinion. For women, i'tikaf is in their home prayer area. I'tikaf is divided into three categories: obligatory if vowed, sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah for the last ten days of Ramadan, and mustahabb at other times. Fasting is only a condition for obligatory i'tikaf, not for voluntary. The minimum duration for voluntary i'tikaf is a short period, even just passing through. The passage then discusses that one may exit for lawful needs. A dispute from Abu Yusuf is noted: he requires congregational mosque only for obligatory i'tikaf, while the chosen opinion requires it for all. The evidence for i'tikaf being sunnah is derived from the Prophet's consistent practice and the lack of disapproval from Companions who did not do it, indicating it is a communal sunnah. The condition of fasting for obligatory i'tikaf is justified by analogy: nights are dependent on days, and the impossibility of fasting at night drops the condition, similar to the prayer of a mustahadah.

Key Terms
الصوم شرط لصحة المنذور (al-sawm shart li-sihhat al-mandhur): Fasting is a condition for the validity of vowed i'tikaf.
سنة كفاية (sunnah kifayah): A communal sunnah; if performed by some, the obligation is lifted from all; if abandoned by all, sin incurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence that i'tikaf in the last ten days is sunnah kifayah and not fard?
A) The Prophet never performed i'tikaf.
B) The Prophet performed i'tikaf only once.
C) The Prophet continuously performed i'tikaf without ever abandoning it, and he did not criticize those who omitted it.
D) The Quran commands i'tikaf.

Key Takeaway
Fasting is required only for vowed i'tikaf; the Prophet's consistent practice without reprimand for omission establishes the last ten days' i'tikaf as sunnah kifayah.

Definition and Conditions of I'tikaf
Defines i'tikaf and its location conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of i'tikaf, identify its conditions, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the mosque requirement.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is valid only in a mosque with regular congregational prayers; women may use their home prayer space.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of i'tikaf (spiritual seclusion). The text clarifies that i'tikaf is not simply any stay in a mosque—it requires intent and a mosque where the five daily prayers are held in congregation. We also examine a key intra-Hanafi difference between Imam Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, and the specific rulings for women.

Guided Path
1
Dissect the definition
Identify the three core elements: staying (iqamah), intention (niyyah), and location (mosque with congregation).
The phrase 'bi niyyatihi' makes intention a pillar.
2
Examine the mosque condition
Note the condition: the mosque must have congregational prayers for all five daily prayers. Ask: why is this necessary?
This is the relied-upon view (al-mukhtar) of Abu Hanifah.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf distinguishes between obligatory (wajib) and voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf. Contrast his position with Abu Hanifah's uniform requirement.
The practical consequence: a vow (nadhr) to perform i'tikaf in a non-congregational mosque is valid according to Abu Yusuf but invalid according to Abu Hanifah.
4
Apply the women's ruling
For women, the valid location is her designated prayer space at home (masjid baytiha). Leaving without excuse invalidates wajib i'tikaf and ends nafl i'tikaf. If she goes to the mosque, it is makruh tanzihan.
The later authorities strongly discourage women from i'tikaf in the mosque.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاعتكاف أحكام الاعتكاف هو الإقامة بنيته في مسجد تقام فيه الجماعة بالفعل للصلوات الخمس، فلا يصح في مسجد لا تقام فيه الجماعة للصلاة على المختار وعن أبي يوسف الاعتكاف الواجب لا يجوز في غير مسجد الجماعة، والنفل يجوز. مراقي الفلاح: ٦٩٩] في مسجد بيتها ولا تخرج منه إذا اعتكفت فلو خرجت لغير عذر يفسد واجبه، وينتهي نفله، ولو اعتكفت في المسجد فظاهرُ ما في "النهاية" أنه يكره تنزيهاً، وينبغي على قياس ما صرحوا به من أن المختار منعهنّ من الخروج في الصلوات كلها أن لا يتردد في منعهن من الاعتكاف في المسجد. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٩٩]
Chapter of I'tikaf. Rulings of I'tikaf: It is staying with intention in a mosque where congregation is actually held for the five prayers. It is not valid in a mosque where congregation is not held for prayer according to the chosen view. And from Abu Yusuf: obligatory i'tikaf is not permissible in a non-congregational mosque, but voluntary i'tikaf is permissible. [Maraqi al-Falah: 699] In her home prayer space: she should not leave it when she performs i'tikaf. If she leaves without an excuse, her obligatory i'tikaf becomes invalid, and her voluntary i'tikaf ends. And if she performs i'tikaf in the mosque, what is apparent from al-Nihayah is that it is slightly disliked (makruh tanzihan). And it should be, on the basis of what they explicitly stated that the chosen view is to prevent women from going out for all prayers, that there should be no hesitation in preventing them from i'tikaf in the mosque. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 699]
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage defines i'tikaf (spiritual seclusion) and its conditions. The definition states that i'tikaf consists of staying in a mosque with the specific intention (niyyah). The mosque must be one where the five daily prayers are held in congregation regularly. If the mosque does not have regular congregational prayers, i'tikaf is not valid according to the relied-upon view (al-mukhtar), which is the position of Abu Hanifah. The text then mentions a narration from Abu Yusuf who distinguishes between obligatory (nadhr) and voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf: obligatory i'tikaf is not valid in a non-congregational mosque, but voluntary i'tikaf is allowed. This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement. The passage then addresses women's i'tikaf: a woman should perform i'tikaf in her designated prayer area at home (masjid baytiha). If she leaves this area without a valid excuse, her obligatory i'tikaf becomes invalid and her voluntary i'tikaf ends. If she chooses to perform i'tikaf in the mosque, it is considered makruh tanzihan (slightly disliked) according to al-Nihayah. The commentary reinforces that the preferred view is to prevent women from i'tikaf in mosques altogether, based on the principle that they are also prevented from attending congregational prayers.

Key Terms
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): Spiritual seclusion in a mosque with intention for worship
مسجد الجماعة (masjid al-jama'ah): A mosque where the five daily prayers are held in congregation regularly
مسجد بيتها (masjid baytiha): A place in a woman's home designated for prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It must be the Masjid al-Haram in Makkah
B) It must have regular congregational prayers for all five daily prayers
C) It can be any mosque, even if prayers are not held there
D) It must be a mosque with a minaret

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf requires a mosque with regular congregational prayers; for women, the home prayer space is recommended and mosque i'tikaf is disliked.

Sawm — Fasting

Types of I'tikaf and the Condition of Fasting
Classifies i'tikaf and states the fasting condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify i'tikaf into its three types and state which type requires fasting as a condition for validity.

Core Idea
Fasting is only required for vowed i'tikaf; voluntary i'tikaf can be as short as a moment.

I'tikaf is a spiritual retreat in the mosque. Islamic law classifies it into three categories based on obligation and time. A common confusion is whether fasting is always required. This passage clarifies that fasting is a condition only for a vowed i'tikaf, not for the sunnah or recommended ones. It also addresses how to handle the night when fasting is impossible and defines the minimum duration for voluntary i'tikaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Types
Read the first sentence. The text divides i'tikaf into three types: wajib (vowed), sunnah kifayah (last ten days of Ramadan), and mustahabb (any other time).
The vowed i'tikaf becomes obligatory upon making a nadhr (vow).
2
Understand the Basis for Sunnah Kifayah
The commentary by al-Zahidi explains why the last ten days are sunnah kifayah: the Prophet continuously performed it but did not rebuke those who omitted it.
Continuous practice without rebuke indicates sunnah, not individual obligation.
3
Learn the Fasting Condition
The text explicitly states that fasting is a condition only for the validity of the vowed i'tikaf. For the other types, fasting is not required.
If someone vows i'tikaf without fasting, they must still fast because the vow implies the condition.
4
Resolve the Night Issue
An objection: if fasting is a condition, why can i'tikaf begin at night when there is no fasting? The answer: conditions are applied according to possibility; night fasting is impossible, so it is excused, and nights follow days.
This is similar to the right of way in a sale or the prayer of a woman with istihadah.
5
Know the Minimum Duration
The minimum for voluntary i'tikaf is undefined – it can be a short stay with intention, even if walking through the mosque. A trick is to intend i'tikaf when entering and exiting to avoid using the mosque as a thoroughfare.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that a mere passing with intention suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاعتكاف على ثلاثة أقسام: واجب في المنذور، وسنة كفاية مؤكدة في العشر الأخير من رمضان ومستحب فيما سواه، والصوم شرط لصحة المنذور فقط، وأقله نفلا مدة يسيرة ولو كان ماشياً على المفتى به. وسنة كفاية إلخ قال الزاهدي: عجباً للناس كيف تركوا الاعتكاف، وقد كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يفعل الشيء ويتركه، ولم يترك الاعتكاف منذ دخل المدينة إلى أن مات فهذه المواظبة المقرونة بعدم الترك مرة لما اقترنت بعدم الإنكار على من لم يفعله من الصحابة من كانت دليل السنية، أي على الكفاية، وإلا كانت دليل الوجوب على الأعيان. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۷۰۰] فيما سواه أي في أي وقت شاء سوى العشر الأخير، ولم يكن منذوراً. مراقي الفلاح: ۷۰۱] لصحة المنذور فلو قال عليّ أن أعتكف شهراً بغير صوم عليه أن يعتكف ويصوم، فإن قيل: لو كان شرطا لكان شرط انعقاد ودوام ، وليس كذلك ؛ لصحة الشروع فيه ليلا وكذا يبقى في الليل ولا صوم؟ قلنا: الشرائط إنما تعتبر بحسب الإمكان ولا إمكان في الليل فيسقط للتعذر وجعلت الليالي تابعة للأيام كالشرب والطريق في بيع الأرض، ألا ترى أن صلاة المستحاضة تصح مع السيلان، وإن عدم الشرط للتعذر، وكذا الخروج والبول لا ينافيه للعجز مع أن الركن أقوى من الشرط. (كفاية) وحاشية الطحطاوي يسيرة: غير محددة، فيحصل بمجرد المكث مع النية. [مراقي الفلاح: ۷۰۲] ماشياً: أي ماراً غير جالس في المسجد ولو ليلاً، وهو حيلة من أراد الدخول والخروج من باب آخر في المسجد حتى لا يجعله طريقاً. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧٠٢]
And i'tikaf is of three types: obligatory (wajib) in what is vowed, sunnah of sufficiency (sunnah kifayah) emphasized in the last ten days of Ramadan, and recommended (mustahabb) in other than that. Fasting is a condition for the validity of the vowed one only. The minimum for voluntary i'tikaf is a short period, even if one is walking, according to the relied-upon position. [Commentary: "Sunnah kifayah etc." al-Zahidi said: "Amazing are the people how they have abandoned i'tikaf. The Messenger of Allah (saws) would do something and leave it, but he never abandoned i'tikaf from the time he entered Madinah until he died. This continuous practice without ever omitting, coupled with the fact that he did not rebuke the Companions who did not do it, indicates that it is sunnah (i.e., on sufficiency). Otherwise, it would indicate individual obligation." [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 700] "In other than that" means in any time one wishes except the last ten days and unless it is vowed. [Maraqi al-Falah: 701] "For the validity of the vowed": if one says, "I vow to observe i'tikaf for a month without fasting," he must observe i'tikaf and fast. If it is said: if it were a condition, it would be a condition for commencement and continuance, but it is not so because it is valid to begin at night, and similarly one remains during the night without fasting. We say: conditions are considered according to possibility, and there is no possibility at night, so it is dropped due to impossibility, and the nights are made to follow the days, like the right to drink water and path in the sale of land. Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage classifies i'tikaf into three categories: (1) Wajib (obligatory) – when one makes a vow (nadhr) to perform i'tikaf; (2) Sunnah kifayah (sufficing sunnah) – highly recommended in the last ten days of Ramadan; (3) Mustahabb (recommended) – at any other time. The commentary from al-Zahidi explains why the last ten days are sunnah kifayah: the Prophet's continuous practice without rebuking those who omitted it shows it is not individually obligatory. Fasting is a condition only for the vowed i'tikaf. If someone vows i'tikaf without fasting, he must still fast because the vow implies the condition. The text then responds to an objection: if fasting is a condition, why can i'tikaf start at night (when no fasting occurs)? The answer: conditions are applied as far as possible; night cannot be fasted, so it is excused. The minimum duration for voluntary i'tikaf is undefined – even a moment of staying with intention suffices, even if walking through the mosque. The commentary notes a trick: one may intend i'tikaf while entering and exiting through different doors so as not to treat the mosque as a through road.

Key Terms
المنذور (al-mandhur): The vowed i'tikaf that becomes obligatory upon the person
سنة كفاية (sunnah kifayah): A sunnah that if performed by some suffices for the community; if abandoned by all, it is blameworthy

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Sunnah kifayah in the last ten days
B) Mustahabb at any time
C) Vowed (mandhur) i'tikaf
D) All types require fasting

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf is classified into three types, and fasting is a condition only for the validity of a vowed (mandhur) i'tikaf.

Permissible Exits, Nullifiers, and Prohibited Acts in I'tikaf
Lists valid exits, nullifying acts, and prohibited actions during i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid exits, nullifying acts, and disliked actions in i'tikaf and state the ruling for each.

Core Idea
Sexual intercourse invalidates i'tikaf; exiting without a valid excuse breaks it; silence as worship is disliked.

I'tikaf requires staying in the mosque with intention. However, certain exits are permitted, while others invalidate the act. This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies which actions are allowed, which are nullifiers, and which are disliked. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly observing i'tikaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify permissible exits
List the valid excuses for leaving the mosque: relieving oneself, being forcibly removed, family dispersal, fear for life or property.
These exits require immediate entry into another mosque.
2
Recognize invalidating exits
Exiting without a valid excuse invalidates obligatory i'tikaf and ends voluntary i'tikaf. Even some excuses like attending a funeral do not save from invalidation.
The text specifically says funeral of a relative or wife invalidates.
3
Identify nullifiers
Sexual intercourse and seminal emission due to its preliminaries invalidate i'tikaf, whether intentional, forgetful, or coerced.
Intercourse is haram and a major nullifier.
4
Understand disliked acts
Observing silence if believed to be worship is disliked (makruh). Transactions for trade are also disliked.
Silence for rest is not disliked.
5
Apply to scenarios
Given a scenario, determine if the i'tikaf remains valid or is invalidated based on the action performed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للغائط  أحكام الاعتكاف المكابرين، من وإخراج ظالم كرهاً، وتفرق أهله، وخوف على نفسه أو متاعه فيدخل مسجدا غيره من ساعته، فإن خرج ساعة بلا عذر فسد الواجب، وانتهى به غيره، وأكل المعتكف وشربه ونومه وعقده البيع لما يحتاجه لنفسه أو عياله في المسجد، خبر مبتدأ تحريما وكره إحضار المبيع فيه وكره عقد ما كان للتجارة، وكره الصمت إن اعتقده قربة والتكلم إلا بخير. وحرم الوطء ودواعيه وبطل بوطئه، وبالإنزال بدواعيه، ولزمته الليالي أيضا بنذر الاعتكاف اعتكاف أيام ولزمته الأيام بنذر الليالي متتابعة وإن لم يشترط التتابع فيدخل حال من الأيام وصلية أي كما لزمته الأيام مسجداً إلخ يريد أن لا يكون خروجه إلا ليعتكف في غيره، ولا يشتغل إلا بالذهاب إلى المسجد الآخر. [ مراقي الفلاح: ۷۰۳] بلا عذر أطلقه وهو مقيد بعذر معتبر في عدم الفساد، فلو خرج لجنازة محرمه أو زوجته فسد؛ لأنه وإن كان عذراً إلا أنه لم يعتبر في عدم الفساد [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٠٣] للتجارة: أطلقها فشملت ما إذا كان المبيع حاضراً في المسجد أو لا. وكره الصمت وهو ترك التحدث مع الناس من غير عذر، وقد ورد النهي عنه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧٠٤] إن اعتقده إلخ أما إذا لم يعتقده قربة فيه، ولكنه حفظ لسانه عن النطق بما لا يفيد فلا بأس به. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧٠٤] اعتقده قربة: أي يكره إذا اعتقده قربةً، فأما للاستراحة ليس بمكروه، ثم قيل : معنى الصمت أن ينذر أن لا يتكلم أصلاً كما كان في شريعة من قبلنا، وقيل: أن يصمت ولا يتكلم أصلاً من غير نذر سابق، وقيل: معناه أن ينوي الصوم المعهود، وهو الإمساك عن المفطرات الثلاث مع زيادة نية أن لا يتكلم. وحرم الوطء: لا يقال: كيف يتهيأ له الوطء وهو في المسجد؛ لأنا نقول: جاز للمعتكف الخروج للحاجة الإنسانية، فعند ذلك أيضاً محرم عليه الوطء حتى يفسد اعتكافه [الكفاية: ۳۱۳/۲] وأقول: أو هو محمول على المرأة تعتكف في مسجد بيتها فيتهيأ له الوطء. وبطل بوطئه أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان عامداً أو ناسياً أو مكرهاً، ليلاً أو نهاراً. For defecation. [Page 226] Rulings of i'tikaf for the obstinate? From: being forcibly removed by a tyrant, dispersal of his family, fear for himself or his property - then he enters another mosque immediately. If he leaves for an hour without excuse, the obligatory (i'tikaf) becomes invalid, and by other (excuses) it ends? The eating, drinking, sleeping of the one in i'tikaf, and his concluding a sale for what he needs for himself or his family in the mosque, (it is permissible as) a subject of predicate indicating prohibition? And it is disliked (makruh) to bring the sold item into the mosque, and it is disliked to conclude a transaction for trade, and it is disliked to observe silence if he believes it to be an act of worship, and (it is recommended) to speak only good. [Maraqi al-Falah: 703] "Without excuse" – it is unrestricted but is restricted to an excuse considered valid for non-invalidity. If he leaves for the funeral of a relative or his wife, it becomes invalid because even though it is an excuse, it is not considered for non-invalidity. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 703] "For trade" – it is unrestricted, including whether the sold item is present in the mosque or not. And silence is disliked, which is refraining from speaking to people without an excuse; the prohibition has been narrated. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/476] But he should occupy himself with reciting Quran, dhikr, hadith, learning and teaching, the Prophet's biography, stories of prophets, accounts of righteous, and writing religious matters. [Maraqi al-Falah: 704] "If he believes it etc." – if he does not believe it to be worship, but merely restrains his tongue from useless talk, there is no harm. [Maraqi al-Falah: 704] "Believed it to be worship" means it is disliked if he believes it to be worship; for rest it is not disliked. Then it is said: the meaning of silence is that he vows not to speak at all, as in previous religions; or that he remains silent without a prior vow; or that he intends typical fasting, abstaining from the three nullifiers with the additional intention of not speaking. And intercourse is forbidden: it should not be asked how it is possible for him while in the mosque, because we say: the person in i'tikaf is permitted to exit for a human need, so at that time also intercourse is forbidden to him such that it invalidates his i'tikaf. [al-Kifayah 2/313] And I say: or it is interpreted as a woman who performs i'tikaf in her home prayer space, so intercourse is possible. And it becomes invalid by intercourse – it is unrestricted, including whether intentional, forgetful, or coerced, night or day. [Maraqi al-Falah: 705] "And the nights are incumbent" – meaning if someone says, "I vow to observe i'tikaf for ten days," then ten consecutive nights are also incumbent; similarly if he says ten nights, then ten consecutive days are incumbent, whether he stipulates consecutiveness or not.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage covers various practical rulings of i'tikaf. It lists permissible exits: for relieving oneself, being forcibly removed, family dispersal, fear for life or property – in such cases one may enter another mosque immediately. An exit without a valid excuse invalidates obligatory i'tikaf and ends voluntary i'tikaf. The commentary specifies that even some excuses (like attending a relative's funeral) are not considered valid to save i'tikaf from invalidation. Eating, drinking, sleeping, and buying necessities in the mosque are permissible. However, bringing the purchased item into the mosque is disliked (makruh). Transactions for trade (not personal need) are also disliked. Observing silence (al-samt) is disliked if one believes it to be an act of worship; otherwise it is not. The proper occupation during i'tikaf is recitation, dhikr, study, etc. Sexual intercourse and its preliminaries are haram and invalidate i'tikaf, regardless of intention, memory, or coercion. The text also addresses how intercourse could occur despite being in the mosque: one may exit for a need, or it applies to a woman in her home space. Finally, for vowed i'tikaf, if one vows days, the nights are also included consecutively, and vice versa, even without stipulation.

Key Terms
الوطء (al-wat'): Sexual intercourse, which invalidates i'tikaf
الصمت (al-samt): Observing silence, which is disliked if believed to be worship
التتابع (al-tatabu'): Consecutiveness of days/nights in vowed i'tikaf

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which exit invalidates obligatory i'tikaf according to the Hanafi school?
A) Leaving for a funeral of a relative
B) Leaving due to fear of property loss
C) Leaving for a human need (toilet)
D) Leaving to enter another mosque because of family dispersal

Key Takeaway
Sexual intercourse invalidates i'tikaf; valid exits are limited to specific excuses; silence as worship is disliked.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Consecutiveness in Vowed I'tikaf (Nadhr)
Ruling on consecutiveness in vowed i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that vow of days includes nights (and vice versa) consecutively, and apply it to examples.

Core Idea
Vowing days automatically includes nights, and vice versa, consecutively.

When one vows i'tikaf for a specified number of days or nights, the Hanafi school requires consecutive observance of both days and nights, even if not stipulated. This passage from Nur al-Idah explains this ruling and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the vow scenario
Determine whether the person vowed i'tikaf for a number of days or a number of nights.
E.g., 'I vow to perform i'tikaf for ten days.'
2
Apply the rule
If days are vowed, nights are also incumbent; if nights are vowed, days are also incumbent.
The obligation is automatic and includes the opposite period.
3
Recognize consecutiveness
The days and nights must be consecutive (mutatabi'ah), even if not stipulated.
Breaking consecutiveness may invalidate the vow.
4
Understand the rationale
I'tikaf inherently requires continuous stay; days cannot be observed without the intervening nights.
The text says 'as the days are incumbent' meaning the stay is continuous.
5
Apply to examples
Given a vow, determine the full obligation: e.g., vow of 5 days implies 5 days and 5 consecutive nights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للغائط  أحكام الاعتكاف المكابرين، من وإخراج ظالم كرهاً، وتفرق أهله، وخوف على نفسه أو متاعه فيدخل مسجدا غيره من ساعته، فإن خرج ساعة بلا عذر فسد الواجب، وانتهى به غيره، وأكل المعتكف وشربه ونومه وعقده البيع لما يحتاجه لنفسه أو عياله في المسجد، خبر مبتدأ تحريما وكره إحضار المبيع فيه وكره عقد ما كان للتجارة، وكره الصمت إن اعتقده قربة والتكلم إلا بخير. وحرم الوطء ودواعيه وبطل بوطئه، وبالإنزال بدواعيه، ولزمته الليالي أيضا بنذر الاعتكاف اعتكاف أيام ولزمته الأيام بنذر الليالي متتابعة وإن لم يشترط التتابع فيدخل حال من الأيام وصلية أي كما لزمته الأيام مسجداً إلخ يريد أن لا يكون خروجه إلا ليعتكف في غيره، ولا يشتغل إلا بالذهاب إلى المسجد الآخر. [ مراقي الفلاح: ۷۰۳] بلا عذر أطلقه وهو مقيد بعذر معتبر في عدم الفساد، فلو خرج لجنازة محرمه أو زوجته فسد؛ لأنه وإن كان عذراً إلا أنه لم يعتبر في عدم الفساد [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٠٣] للتجارة: أطلقها فشملت ما إذا كان المبيع حاضراً في المسجد أو لا. وكره الصمت وهو ترك التحدث مع الناس من غير عذر، وقد ورد النهي عنه. [البحر الرائق: ٤٧٦/٢] ولكنه يلازم قراءة القرآن والذكر والحديث، والعلم ودراسته، وسير النبي وقصص الأنبياء وحكاية الصالحين، وكتابة أمور الدين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧٠٤] إن اعتقده إلخ أما إذا لم يعتقده قربة فيه، ولكنه حفظ لسانه عن النطق بما لا يفيد فلا بأس به. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧٠٤] اعتقده قربة: أي يكره إذا اعتقده قربةً، فأما للاستراحة ليس بمكروه، ثم قيل : معنى الصمت أن ينذر أن لا يتكلم أصلاً كما كان في شريعة من قبلنا، وقيل: أن يصمت ولا يتكلم أصلاً من غير نذر سابق، وقيل: معناه أن ينوي الصوم المعهود، وهو الإمساك عن المفطرات الثلاث مع زيادة نية أن لا يتكلم. وحرم الوطء: لا يقال: كيف يتهيأ له الوطء وهو في المسجد؛ لأنا نقول: جاز للمعتكف الخروج للحاجة الإنسانية، فعند ذلك أيضاً محرم عليه الوطء حتى يفسد اعتكافه [الكفاية: ۳۱۳/۲] وأقول: أو هو محمول على المرأة تعتكف في مسجد بيتها فيتهيأ له الوطء. وبطل بوطئه أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان عامداً أو ناسياً أو مكرهاً، ليلاً أو نهاراً. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧٠٥] ولزمته الليالي: أي ومن قال علي أن أعتكف عشرة أيام مثلاً، تلزمه عشرة ليال متتابعةً أيضاً، وكذا إذا قال: علي أن أعتكف عشرة ليال مثلاً، تلزمه عشرة أيام متتابعة أيضاً، سواء اشترط التتابع أو لم يشترط.
For defecation. [Page 226] Rulings of i'tikaf for the obstinate? From: being forcibly removed by a tyrant, dispersal of his family, fear for himself or his property - then he enters another mosque immediately. If he leaves for an hour without excuse, the obligatory (i'tikaf) becomes invalid, and by other (excuses) it ends? The eating, drinking, sleeping of the one in i'tikaf, and his concluding a sale for what he needs for himself or his family in the mosque, (it is permissible as) a subject of predicate indicating prohibition? And it is disliked (makruh) to bring the sold item into the mosque, and it is disliked to conclude a transaction for trade, and it is disliked to observe silence if he believes it to be an act of worship, and (it is recommended) to speak only good. And sexual intercourse and its preliminaries are forbidden (haram), and i'tikaf becomes invalid by intercourse, and by seminal emission due to its preliminaries. Also, the nights are incumbent (lazima) with a vow of i'tikaf of days, and the days are incumbent with a vow of nights, consecutively, even if he did not stipulate consecutiveness. So he enters a state of days? As the days are incumbent? The explanation: he intends that his exit is only to perform i'tikaf in another mosque, and he is not occupied except with going to the other mosque. [Maraqi al-Falah: 703] "Without excuse" – it is unrestricted but is restricted to an excuse considered valid for non-invalidity. If he leaves for the funeral of a relative or his wife, it becomes invalid because even though it is an excuse, it is not considered for non-invalidity. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 703] "For trade" – it is unrestricted, including whether the sold item is present in the mosque or not. And silence is disliked, which is refraining from speaking to people without an excuse; the prohibition has been narrated. [Maraqi al-Falah: 704] "If he believes it etc." – if he does not believe it to be worship, but merely restrains his tongue from useless talk, there is no harm. [Maraqi al-Falah: 704] "Believed it to be worship" means it is disliked if he believes it to be worship; for rest it is not disliked. Then it is said: the meaning of silence is that he vows not to speak at all, as in previous religions; or that he remains silent without a prior vow; or that he intends typical fasting, abstaining from the three nullifiers with the additional intention of not speaking. And intercourse is forbidden: it should not be asked how it is possible for him while in the mosque, because we say: the person in i'tikaf is permitted to exit for a human need, so at that time also intercourse is forbidden to him such that it invalidates his i'tikaf. And it becomes invalid by intercourse – it is unrestricted, including whether intentional, forgetful, or coerced, night or day. Commentary
This passage covers various practical rulings of i'tikaf. It lists permissible exits: for relieving oneself, being forcibly removed, family dispersal, fear for life or property – in such cases one may enter another mosque immediately. Key Terms
التتابع (al-tatabu'): Consecutiveness of days/nights in vowed i'tikaf

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when someone vows i'tikaf for 10 days without mentioning nights?
A) Only 10 days are required; nights are optional
B) 10 days and 10 nights are required, but not necessarily consecutive
C) 10 days and 10 consecutive nights are required
D) The vow is invalid because nights must be specified

Key Takeaway
Vowed i'tikaf of days automatically includes consecutive nights, and vows of nights automatically include consecutive days.
